\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-AddTimer@{SDL\_\-AddTimer}}
\index{SDL\_\-AddTimer@{SDL\_\-AddTimer}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-AddTimer}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static {\bf SDL\_\-TimerID} SDL\_\-AddTimer (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{int}]{ interval, }
\item[{SDL\_\-NewTimerCallback}]{ callback}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a0847fd552fc17aa314f866ac16db60df}


Add a timer which will call a callback after the specified number of milliseconds has elapsed. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em callback}]The callback to run. \item[{\em interval}]The timer interval. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns an ID value for the added timer or NULL if there was an error. 
\end{DoxyReturn}


Adds a callback function to be run after the specified number of milliseconds has elapsed. The callback function is passed the current timer interval and the user supplied parameter from the SDL\_\-AddTimer call and returns the next timer interval. If the returned value from the callback is the same as the one passed in, the periodic alarm continues, otherwise a new alarm is scheduled. 

To cancel a currently running timer call \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a135aaf0e0425b1dcf1904b966509c3c0}{SDL\_\-RemoveTimer} with the timer ID returned from SDL\_\-AddTimer. 

The timer callback function may run in a different thread than your main program, and so shouldn't call any functions from within itself. You may always call SDL\_\-PushEvent, however. 

The granularity of the timer is platform-\/dependent, but you should count on it being at least 10 ms as this is the most common number. This means that if you request a 16 ms timer, your callback will run approximately 20 ms later on an unloaded system. If you wanted to set a flag signaling a frame update at 30 frames per second (every 33 ms), you might set a timer for 30 ms (see example below). If you use this function, you need to pass SDL\_\-INIT\_\-TIMER to SDL\_\-Init(int). 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-timer.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
extern DECLSPEC SDL_TimerID SDLCALL 
                SDL_AddTimer(Uint32 interval, 
                SDL_NewTimerCallback callback, void *param)
\end{DoxyCode}
  \hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_a0084f0508a98488790b16db0ec6324f5}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-AddTimer@{SDL\_\-AddTimer}}
\index{SDL\_\-AddTimer@{SDL\_\-AddTimer}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}

The timer callback function may run in a different thread than your main program, and so shouldn't call any functions from within itself. You may always call SDL\_\-PushEvent, however. 

The granularity of the timer is platform-\/dependent, but you should count on it being at least 10 ms as this is the most common number. This means that if you request a 16 ms timer, your callback will run approximately 20 ms later on an unloaded system. \label{_sdl_8cs_aa1fe24060926a8679b4a16201728a1e9}


Allocates an empty, unpopulated SDL\_\-RWops structure. 

SDL\_\-AllocRW allocates an empty, unpopulated SDL\_\-RWops structure. You must fill out the fields yourself. \begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns a pointer to the allocated memory on success, or NULL on error. 

You must free any memory allocated with \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_aa1fe24060926a8679b4a16201728a1e9}{SDL\_\-AllocRW} with \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a13c12ec9d6bfe668b50e13cb71ebd8ee}{SDL\_\-FreeRW}. Depending on your operating system and compiler, there may be a difference between the malloc() and free() your program uses and the versions SDL calls internally. Trying to mix the two can cause crashing such as segmentation faults.
\end{DoxyReturn}

\index{SDL\_\-BlitSurface@{SDL\_\-BlitSurface}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-BlitSurface}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-BlitSurface (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{IntPtr}]{ src, }
\item[{ref {\bf SDL\_\-Rect}}]{ srcrect, }
\item[{IntPtr}]{ dst, }
\item[{ref {\bf SDL\_\-Rect}}]{ dstrect}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_aec41f77b04d717457433acbecd7a257b}


This performs a fast blit from the source surface to the destination surface. 

This performs a fast blit from the source surface to the destination surface. 

The width and height in srcrect determine the size of the copied rectangle. Only the position is used in the dstrect (the width and height are ignored). 

If srcrect is NULL, the entire surface is copied. If dstrect is NULL, then the destination position (upper left corner) is (0, 0). 

The final blit rectangle is saved in dstrect after all clipping is performed (srcrect is not modified). 

The blit function should not be called on a locked surface. 

The results of blitting operations vary greatly depending on whether SDL\_\-SRCAPLHA is set or not. See SDL\_\-SetAlpha for an explaination of how this affects your results. Colorkeying and alpha attributes also interact with surface blitting, as the following pseudo-\/code should hopefully explain.  
\begin{DoxyCode}
if (source surface has SDL_SRCALPHA set) 
                {
                        if (source surface has alpha channel (that is, format->Am
      ask != 0))
                        blit using per-pixel alpha, ignoring any colour key
                        else {
                        if (source surface has SDL_SRCCOLORKEY set)
                                blit using the colour key AND the per-surface alp
      ha value
                        else
                                blit using the per-surface alpha value
                        }
           } 
           else 
           {
           if (source surface has SDL_SRCCOLORKEY set)
           blit using the colour key
           else
           ordinary opaque rectangular blit
           }
\end{DoxyCode}
 p$>$Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: code$>$int SDL\_\-BlitSurface(SDL\_\-Surface $\ast$src, SDL\_\-Rect $\ast$srcrect, SDL\_\-Surface $\ast$dst, SDL\_\-Rect $\ast$dstrect); /code$>$


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em src}]IntPtr to \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___surface}{SDL\_\-Surface}\item[{\em srcrect}]IntPtr to \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___rect}{SDL\_\-Rect}\item[{\em dst}]IntPtr to \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___surface}{SDL\_\-Surface}\item[{\em dstrect}]IntPtr to \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___rect}{SDL\_\-Rect}\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
If the blit is successful, it returns 0, otherwise it returns -\/1. 

If either of the surfaces were in video memory, and the blit returns -\/2, the video memory was lost, so it should be reloaded with artwork and re-\/blitted: 


\begin{DoxyCode}
while ( SDL_BlitSurface(image, imgrect, screen, dstrect) == -2 ) 
                {
                        while ( SDL_LockSurface(image)) &lt; 0 )
                        SDL_Delay(10);
                        -- Write image pixels to image-&gt;pixels --
                        SDL_UnlockSurface(image);
                }
\end{DoxyCode}
 

This happens under DirectX 5.0 when the system switches away from your fullscreen application. Locking the surface will also fail until you have access to the video memory again. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_afae9570bf3fb2b26f7403cb1fc4f1353}{SDL\_\-LockSurface}, \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_ac5e42937782d41622cec743f145b4f81}{SDL\_\-FillRect(IntPtr, ref SDL\_\-Rect, int)}, \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___surface}{SDL\_\-Surface}, \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___rect}{SDL\_\-Rect}


\end{DoxySeeAlso}

Initializes a SDL\_\-AudioCVT structure for conversion. 

Before an SDL\_\-AudioCVT structure can be used to convert audio data it must be initialized with source and destination information. 

src\_\-format and dst\_\-format are the source and destination format of the conversion. (For information on audio formats see SDL\_\-AudioSpec). src\_\-channels and dst\_\-channels are the number of channels in the source and destination formats. Finally, src\_\-rate and dst\_\-rate are the frequency or samples-\/per-\/second of the source and destination formats. Once again, see SDL\_\-AudioSpec. 


\begin{DoxyCode}
            int SDL_BuildAudioCVT(SDL_AudioCVT *cvt, Uint16 src_format, Uint8 src
      _channels, int src_rate, Uint16 dst_format, Uint8 dst_channels, int dst_rate)
\end{DoxyCode}


See \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a7ed641a1e339dc97cfd58c08dd9af2e2}{SDL\_\-ConvertAudio}.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns -\/1 if the filter could not be built or 1 if it could.

\label{_sdl_8cs_a66f1e7b4fe4df8529b3afd7c3600d7bc}


Returns a human-\/readable, system-\/dependent identifier for the CD-\/ROM. 

Drive is the index of the drive. Drive indices start to 0 and end at \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a4610e2722bd3b4c4951ab3c18f4f9a6f}{SDL\_\-CDNumDrives()}-\/1. 

Binds to C-\/function in SDL\_\-cdrom.h 
\begin{DoxyCode}
const char *SDL_CDName(int drive);
\end{DoxyCode}


Example: \char`\"{}/dev/cdrom\char`\"{} \char`\"{}E:\char`\"{} \char`\"{}/dev/disk/ide/1/master\char`\"{} 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}

\label{_sdl_8cs_a8ce19531378969ac823e35d181c1079d}


Opens a CD-\/ROM drive for access. 

Opens a CD-\/ROM drive for access. It returns a SDL\_\-CD structure on success, or NULL if the drive was invalid or busy. This newly opened CD-\/ROM becomes the default CD used when other CD functions are passed a NULL CD-\/ROM handle. 

Drives are numbered starting with 0. Drive 0 is the system default CD-\/ROM. 

Binds to C-\/function in SDL\_\-cdrom.h 
\begin{DoxyCode}
SDL_CD *SDL_CDOpen(int drive)
\end{DoxyCode}



\begin{DoxyCode}
            SDL_CD *cdrom;
                        int cur_track;
                        int min, sec, frame;
                        SDL_Init(SDL_INIT_CDROM);
                        atexit(SDL_Quit);

                        /* Check for CD drives */
                        if(!SDL_CDNumDrives())
                                {
                        /* None found */
                        fprintf(stderr, "No CDROM devices available\n");
                        exit(-1);
                }

                /* Open the default drive */
                cdrom=SDL_CDOpen(0);

                /* Did if open? Check if cdrom is NULL */
                if(!cdrom)
           {
                fprintf(stderr, "Couldn't open drive: %s\n", SDL_GetError());
                exit(-1);
           }

                /* Print Volume info */
                printf("Name: %s\n", SDL_CDName(0));
                printf("Tracks: %d\n", cdrom->numtracks);
                for(cur_track=0;cur_track &lt; cdrom-&gt;numtracks; cur_track++)
           {
                FRAMES_TO_MSF(cdrom->track[cur_track].length, &amp;min, &amp;sec,
       &amp;frame);
                printf("\tTrack %d: Length %d:%d\n", cur_track, min, sec);
           }

           SDL_CDClose(cdrom);
            /code>
            </example>
            <param name="drive"></param>
            <returns>It returns a SDL_CD structure
             on success, or NULL if the drive was invalid or busy.
             </returns>
             <seealso cref="SDL_CD"/>
             <seealso cref="SDL_CDtrack"/>
             <seealso cref="SDL_CDClose"/> */
        [DllImport(SDL_NATIVE_LIBRARY, CallingConvention = CALLING_CONVENTION),
        SuppressUnmanagedCodeSecurity]
        public static extern IntPtr SDL_CDOpen(int drive);

\end{DoxyCode}



\begin{DoxyCode}
            int playTrack(int track)
                {
                        int playing = 0;

                        if ( CD_INDRIVE(SDL_CDStatus(cdrom)) ) 
                {
                        /* clamp to the actual number of tracks on the CD */
                        if (track >= cdrom->numtracks) 
                {
                        track = cdrom->numtracks-1;
                }

                if ( SDL_CDPlayTracks(cdrom, track, 0, 1, 0) == 0 ) 
           {
                playing = 1;
           }
           }
           return playing;
           }
            /code>
            </example>
            <param name="cdrom"></param>
            <returns>CDstatus enum</returns>
            <seealso cref="SDL_CD"/> */
        [DllImport(SDL_NATIVE_LIBRARY, CallingConvention = CALLING_CONVENTION),

        public static extern int SDL_CDStatus(IntPtr cdrom);

\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{IntPtr}]{ cdrom, }

\item[{int}]{ ntracks, }
\item[{int}]{ nframes}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}

\label{_sdl_8cs_aee7740538b0cf769097abc2b21b4945e}


Play the given CD track(s). 

SDL\_\-CDPlayTracks plays the given CD starting at track start\_\-track, for ntracks tracks. 

start\_\-frame is the frame offset, from the beginning of the start\_\-track, at which to start. nframes is the frame offset, from the beginning of the last track (start\_\-track+ntracks), at which to end playing. 

SDL\_\-CDPlayTracks should only be called after calling SDL\_\-CDStatus to get track information about the CD. 

Note: Data tracks are ignored. 

Binds to C-\/function in SDL\_\-cdrom.h 
\begin{DoxyCode}
int SDL_CDPlayTracks(SDL_CD *cdrom, int start_track, int start_frame, int ntracks
      , int nframes))
\end{DoxyCode}



\begin{DoxyCode}
                        /* assuming cdrom is a previously opened device */
                        /* Play the entire CD */
                        if(CD_INDRIVE(SDL_CDStatus(cdrom)))
                        SDL_CDPlayTracks(cdrom, 0, 0, 0, 0);

                        /* Play the first track */
                        if(CD_INDRIVE(SDL_CDStatus(cdrom)))
                        SDL_CDPlayTracks(cdrom, 0, 0, 1, 0);

                        /* Play first 15 seconds of the 2nd track */
                        if(CD_INDRIVE(SDL_CDStatus(cdrom)))
                        SDL_CDPlayTracks(cdrom, 1, 0, 0, CD_FPS*15);
\end{DoxyCode}

  \hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_a7ed641a1e339dc97cfd58c08dd9af2e2}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-ConvertAudio@{SDL\_\-ConvertAudio}}
\index{SDL\_\-ConvertAudio@{SDL\_\-ConvertAudio}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-ConvertAudio}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-ConvertAudio (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{IntPtr}]{ cvt}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a7ed641a1e339dc97cfd58c08dd9af2e2}


Convert audio data to a desired audio format. 

SDL\_\-ConvertAudio takes one parameter, cvt, which was previously initialized. Initilizing a SDL\_\-AudioCVT is a two step process. First of all, the structure must be passed to \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_ab290a18bf5bf8a161042ceb8c43c5654}{SDL\_\-BuildAudioCVT(IntPtr, short, byte, int, short, byte, int)} along with source and destination format parameters. Secondly, the cvt-\/$>$buf and cvt-\/$>$len fields must be setup. cvt-\/$>$buf should point to the audio data and cvt-\/$>$len should be set to the length of the audio data in bytes. Remember, the length of the buffer pointed to by buf show be len$\ast$len\_\-mult bytes in length. 

Once the SDL\_\-AudioCVTstructure is initilized then we can pass it to SDL\_\-ConvertAudio, which will convert the audio data pointer to by cvt-\/$>$buf. If SDL\_\-ConvertAudio returned 0 then the conversion was completed successfully, otherwise -\/1 is returned. 

If the conversion completed successfully then the converted audio data can be read from cvt-\/$>$buf. The amount of valid, converted, audio data in the buffer is equal to cvt-\/$>$len$\ast$cvt-\/$>$len\_\-ratio. 


\begin{DoxyCode}
            int SDL_ConvertAudio(SDL_AudioCVT *cvt)
\end{DoxyCode}



\begin{DoxyCode}
            /* Converting some WAV data to hardware format */
                        void my_audio_callback(void *userdata, Uint8 *stream, int
       len);

                        SDL_AudioSpec *desired, *obtained;
                        SDL_AudioSpec wav_spec;
                        SDL_AudioCVT  wav_cvt;
                        Uint32 wav_len;
                        Uint8 *wav_buf;
                        int ret;

                        /* Allocated audio specs */
                        desired = malloc(sizeof(SDL_AudioSpec));
                        obtained = malloc(sizeof(SDL_AudioSpec));

                        /* Set desired format */
                        desired-&gt;freq=22050;
                        desired-&gt;format=AUDIO_S16LSB;
                        desired-&gt;samples=8192;
                        desired-&gt;callback=my_audio_callback;
                        desired-&gt;userdata=NULL;

                        /* Open the audio device */
                        if ( SDL_OpenAudio(desired, obtained) &lt; 0 )
                {
                        fprintf(stderr, "Couldn't open audio: %s\n", SDL_GetError
      ());
                        exit(-1);
                }

                free(desired);

                /* Load the test.wav */
                if( SDL_LoadWAV("test.wav", &amp;wav_spec, &amp;wav_buf, &amp;wav
      _len) == NULL )
           {
                fprintf(stderr, "Could not open test.wav: %s\n", SDL_GetError());
      
                SDL_CloseAudio();
                free(obtained);
                exit(-1);

                /* Build AudioCVT */
                ret = SDL_BuildAudioCVT(&amp;wav_cvt,
                wav_spec.format, wav_spec.channels, wav_spec.freq,
                obtained-&gt;format, obtained-&gt;channels, obtained-&gt;freq);

                /* Check that the convert was built */
                if(ret==-1)
           {
                fprintf(stderr, "Couldn't build converter!\n");
                SDL_CloseAudio();
                free(obtained);
                SDL_FreeWAV(wav_buf);
           }

                /* Setup for conversion */
                wav_cvt.buf = malloc(wav_len * wav_cvt.len_mult);
                wav_cvt.len = wav_len;
                memcpy(wav_cvt.buf, wav_buf, wav_len);

                /* We can delete to original WAV data now */
                SDL_FreeWAV(wav_buf);

                /* And now we're ready to convert */
                SDL_ConvertAudio(&amp;wav_cvt);

                /* do whatever */
                .
                .
                .
                .
\end{DoxyCode}
 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em cvt}]IntPtr to SDL\_\-AudioCVT struct. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
If SDL\_\-ConvertAudio returned 0 then the conversion was completed successfully, otherwise -\/1 is returned. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
SDL\_\-AudioCVT, \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_ab290a18bf5bf8a161042ceb8c43c5654}{SDL\_\-BuildAudioCVT(IntPtr, short, byte, int, short, byte, int)}


\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\item[{IntPtr}]{ fmt, }
\item[{int}]{ flags}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a120ecaa205cb5d317d43f02e765a963b}


Converts a surface to the same format as another surface. 

Creates a new surface of the specified format, and then copies and maps the given surface to it. If this function fails, it returns NULL. 

The flags parameter is passed to \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_aa732dd717414124c4710c0d25f8e07ce}{SDL\_\-CreateRGBSurface(int, int, int, int, int, int, int, int)} and has those semantics. 

This function is used internally by \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a557565508a6c32f7bb4703f040a622c1}{SDL\_\-DisplayFormat}. 

This function can only be called after SDL\_\-Init. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
            SDL_Surface *SDL_ConvertSurface(SDL_Surface *src, SDL_PixelFormat *fm
      t, Uint32 flags)
\end{DoxyCode}



\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em src}]IntPtr to \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___surface}{SDL\_\-Surface}\item[{\em fmt}]IntPTr to \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___pixel_format}{SDL\_\-PixelFormat}\item[{\em flags}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns either a pointer to the new surface, or NULL on error. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\label{_sdl_8cs_aab5253287140e2324b65aa03519ea6d8}


Creates a new mouse cursor. 

Create a cursor using the specified data and mask (in MSB format). The cursor width must be a multiple of 8 bits. 

The cursor is created in black and white according to the following: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
            data  mask    resulting pixel on screen
             0     1       White
             1     1       Black
             0     0       Transparent
             1     0       Inverted color if possible, black if not.
\end{DoxyCode}
 Cursors created with this function must be freed with \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a9649cb004abe3f8d89f6763387ca3bc4}{SDL\_\-FreeCursor}. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-mouse.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
            SDL_Cursor *SDL_CreateCursor(Uint8 *data, Uint8 *mask, int w, int h, 
      int hot_x, int hot_y);
\end{DoxyCode}
 


\begin{DoxyCode}
            /* Stolen from the mailing list */
 Creates a new mouse cursor from an XPM */

            /* XPM */
           static const char *arrow[] = {
             /* width height num_colors chars_per_pixel */
             "    32    32        3            1",
             /* colors */
            "X c #000000",
             ". c #ffffff",
             "  c None",
             /* pixels */
             "X                               ",
             "XX                              ",
             "X.X                             ",
             "X..X                            ",
             "X...X                           ",
             "X....X                          ",
             "X.....X                         ",
             "X......X                        ",
             "X.......X                       ",
             "X........X                      ",
             "X.....XXXXX                     ",
             "X..X..X                         ",
             "X.X X..X                        ",
             "XX  X..X                        ",
             "X    X..X                       ",
             "     X..X                       ",
             "      X..X                      ",
             "      X..X                      ",
             "       XX                       ",
             "                                ",
             "                                ",
             "                                ",
             "                                ",
             "                                ",
             "                                ",
             "                                ",
             "                                ",
             "                                ",
             "                                ",
             "                                ",
             "                                ",
             "                                ",
             "0,0"
           };

           static SDL_Cursor *init_system_cursor(const char *image[])
           {
             int i, row, col;
             Uint8 data[4*32];
             Uint8 mask[4*32];
             int hot_x, hot_y;

             i = -1;
             for ( row=0; row&lt;32; ++row ) {
               for ( col=0; col&lt;32; ++col ) {
                 if ( col % 8 ) {
                   data[i] &lt;&lt;= 1;
                   mask[i] &lt;&lt;= 1;
                 } else {
                   ++i;
                   data[i] = mask[i] = 0;
                 }
                 switch (image[4+row][col]) {
                   case 'X':
                     data[i] |= 0x01;
                     mask[i] |= 0x01;
                     break;
                   case '.':
                     mask[i] |= 0x01;
                     break;
                   case ' ':
                     break;
                 }
               }
             }
             sscanf(image[4+row], "%d,%d", &amp;hot_x, &amp;hot_y);
             return SDL_CreateCursor(data, mask, 32, 32, hot_x, hot_y);
           }
\end{DoxyCode}
 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em data}]\item[{\em h}]\item[{\em hot\_\-x}]\item[{\em hot\_\-y}]\item[{\em mask}]\item[{\em w}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}

\end{DoxyReturn}

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\label{_sdl_8cs_a09e1892c9d6a02ce0c8b1ff92e032666}


Create an \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___surface}{SDL\_\-Surface} from pixel data. 

Creates an \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___surface}{SDL\_\-Surface} from the provided pixel data. 

The data stored in pixels is assumed to be of the depth specified in the parameter list. The pixel data is not copied into the \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___surface}{SDL\_\-Surface} structure so it should not be freed until the surface has been freed with a called to \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a3062b061d8f75b52d1c4887209a92c10}{SDL\_\-FreeSurface}. pitch is the length of each scanline in bytes.  

See \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_aa732dd717414124c4710c0d25f8e07ce}{SDL\_\-CreateRGBSurface(int, int, int, int, int, int, int, int)} for a more detailed description of the other parameters. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
SDL_Surface *SDL_CreateRGBSurfaceFrom(void *pixels, int width, int height, int de
      pth, int pitch, Uint32 Rmask, Uint32 Gmask, Uint32 Bmask, Uint32 Amask)
\end{DoxyCode}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns the created surface, or NULL upon error. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\label{_sdl_8cs_a433c9c002d6c6a4a3077fc12ff790372}


Create a YUV video overlay. 

SDL\_\-CreateYUVOverlay creates a YUV overlay of the specified width, height and format (see \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___overlay}{SDL\_\-Overlay} for a list of available formats), for the provided display. A \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___overlay}{SDL\_\-Overlay} structure is returned. 

The term 'overlay' is a misnomer since, unless the overlay is created in hardware, the contents for the display surface underneath the area where the overlay is shown will be overwritten when the overlay is displayed. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
SDL_Overlay *SDL_CreateYUVOverlay(int width, int height, Uint32 format, 
      SDL_Surface *display)
\end{DoxyCode}

Wait a specified number of milliseconds before returning. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em ms}]The number of milliseconds to wait. \end{DoxyParams}


{\bfseries SDL\_\-Delay} will wait at least the specified time, but possible longer due to OS scheduling. Count on a delay granularity of at least 10 ms. Some platforms have shorter clock ticks but this is the most common.

\label{_sdl_8cs_a557565508a6c32f7bb4703f040a622c1}


Convert a surface to the display format. 

This function takes a surface and copies it to a new surface of the pixel format and colors of the video framebuffer, suitable for fast blitting onto the display surface. It calls \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a120ecaa205cb5d317d43f02e765a963b}{SDL\_\-ConvertSurface(IntPtr, IntPtr, int)}. 

If you want to take advantage of hardware colorkey or alpha blit acceleration, you should set the colorkey and alpha value before calling this function. 

If you want an alpha channel, see \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_ad76ca477f17f31fd3aaccf8c19f643c1}{SDL\_\-DisplayFormatAlpha}. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
SDL_Surface *SDL_DisplayFormat(SDL_Surface *surface)
\end{DoxyCode}
 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em surface}]IntPtr to \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___surface}{SDL\_\-Surface}\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
IntPtr to \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___surface}{SDL\_\-Surface}. If the conversion fails or runs out of memory, it returns NULL
\end{DoxyReturn}
\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_ad76ca477f17f31fd3aaccf8c19f643c1}{

\index{SDL\_\-DisplayFormatAlpha@{SDL\_\-DisplayFormatAlpha}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}

\begin{DoxyParamCaption}

\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_ad76ca477f17f31fd3aaccf8c19f643c1}


Convert a surface to the display format. 

This function takes a surface and copies it to a new surface of the pixel format and colors of the video framebuffer plus an alpha channel, suitable for fast blitting onto the display surface. It calls \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a120ecaa205cb5d317d43f02e765a963b}{SDL\_\-ConvertSurface(IntPtr, IntPtr, int)}. 

If you want to take advantage of hardware colorkey or alpha blit acceleration, you should set the colorkey and alpha value before calling this function. 

This function can be used to convert a colourkey to an alpha channel, if the SDL\_\-SRCCOLORKEY flag is set on the surface. The generated surface will then be transparent (alpha=0) where the pixels match the colourkey, and opaque (alpha=255) elsewhere. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
SDL_Surface *SDL_DisplayFormatAlpha(SDL_Surface *surface)
\end{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxyReturn}

\label{_sdl_8cs_af31ec1fa8ac9f58ec682d0ae0b363cc8}


Set keyboard repeat rate. 

Enables or disables the keyboard repeat rate. delay specifies how long the key must be pressed before it begins repeating, it then repeats at the speed specified by interval. Both delay and interval are expressed in milliseconds. 

Setting delay to 0 disables key repeating completely. Good default values are SDL\_\-DEFAULT\_\-REPEAT\_\-DELAY and SDL\_\-DEFAULT\_\-REPEAT\_\-INTERVAL. p$>$Binds to C-\/function in SDL\_\-keyboard.h code$>$int \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_af31ec1fa8ac9f58ec682d0ae0b363cc8}{SDL\_\-EnableKeyRepeat(int delay, int interval)}; /code$>$

\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-EnableUNICODE@{SDL\_\-EnableUNICODE}}
\index{SDL\_\-EnableUNICODE@{SDL\_\-EnableUNICODE}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-EnableUNICODE}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-EnableUNICODE (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{int}]{ enable}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a84ff6db83e36f31aa5b5643cc18b1364}


Enable UNICODE translation. 

Enables/Disables Unicode keyboard translation. 

To obtain the character codes corresponding to received keyboard events, Unicode translation must first be turned on using this function. The translation incurs a slight overhead for each keyboard event and is therefore disabled by default. For each subsequently received key down event, the unicode member of the SDL\_\-keysym structure will then contain the corresponding character code, or zero for keysyms that do not correspond to any character code. 

A value of 1 for enable enables Unicode translation; 0 disables it, and -\/1 leaves it unchanged (useful for querying the current translation mode). 

Note that only key press events will be translated, not release events. 

Binds to C-\/function in SDL\_\-keyboard.h 
\begin{DoxyCode}
int SDL_EnableUNICODE(int enable);
\end{DoxyCode}



\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em enable}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns the previous translation mode (0 or 1). 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
SDL\_\-keysym


\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-EventState}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-EventState (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{byte}]{ type, }
\item[{int}]{ state}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a33f65e0690703749dc213ed95b406dd2}


This function allows you to set the state of processing certain events. 

This function allows you to set the state of processing certain event type's. 

If 'state' is set to SDL\_\-IGNORE, that event will be automatically dropped from the event queue and will not be filtered. 

If 'state' is set to SDL\_\-ENABLE, that event will be processed normally. 

If 'state' is set to SDL\_\-QUERY, SDL\_\-EventState will return the current processing state of the specified event type. 

A list of event type's can be found in the SDL\_\-Event section.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em type}]\item[{\em state}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns 0 on success or -\/1 if the event couldn't be pushed. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
SDL\_\-Event


\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_a2be96435f87ccf4bf46776e6b0d30721}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-FillRect@{SDL\_\-FillRect}}
\index{SDL\_\-FillRect@{SDL\_\-FillRect}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-FillRect}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-FillRect (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{IntPtr}]{ surface, }
\item[{ref {\bf SDL\_\-Rect}}]{ rect, }
\item[{uint}]{ color}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a2be96435f87ccf4bf46776e6b0d30721}


This function performs a fast fill of the given rectangle with some color. 

This function performs a fast fill of the given rectangle with color. If dstrect is NULL, the whole surface will be filled with color. 

The color should be a pixel of the format used by the surface, and can be generated by the \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a8c6c5785c9010c08364e8abcd34648a0}{SDL\_\-MapRGB} or \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_aadad00b884d9cab5dcfc16b887963bb3}{SDL\_\-MapRGBA} functions. If the color value contains an alpha value then the destination is simply \char`\"{}filled\char`\"{} with that alpha information, no blending takes place. 

If there is a clip rectangle set on the destination (set via \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a201a7363fdcfe07651a1298a3e4e1778}{SDL\_\-SetClipRect}) then this function will clip based on the intersection of the clip rectangle and the dstrect rectangle and the dstrect rectangle will be modified to represent the area actually filled. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
            int SDL_FillRect(SDL_Surface *dst, SDL_Rect *dstrect, Uint32 color);
\end{DoxyCode}
 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em surface}]IntPtr to \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___surface}{SDL\_\-Surface}\item[{\em rect}]IntPtr to \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___rect}{SDL\_\-Rect}\item[{\em color}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
This function returns 0 on success, or -\/1 on error. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a8c6c5785c9010c08364e8abcd34648a0}{SDL\_\-MapRGB}, \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_aadad00b884d9cab5dcfc16b887963bb3}{SDL\_\-MapRGBA}, \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_aec41f77b04d717457433acbecd7a257b}{SDL\_\-BlitSurface}, \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___rect}{SDL\_\-Rect}


\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_ac5e42937782d41622cec743f145b4f81}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-FillRect@{SDL\_\-FillRect}}
\index{SDL\_\-FillRect@{SDL\_\-FillRect}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-FillRect}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-FillRect (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{IntPtr}]{ surface, }
\item[{ref {\bf SDL\_\-Rect}}]{ rect, }
\item[{int}]{ color}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_ac5e42937782d41622cec743f145b4f81}


This function performs a fast fill of the given rectangle with some color. 

This function performs a fast fill of the given rectangle with color. If dstrect is NULL, the whole surface will be filled with color. 

The color should be a pixel of the format used by the surface, and can be generated by the \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a8c6c5785c9010c08364e8abcd34648a0}{SDL\_\-MapRGB} or \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_aadad00b884d9cab5dcfc16b887963bb3}{SDL\_\-MapRGBA} functions. If the color value contains an alpha value then the destination is simply \char`\"{}filled\char`\"{} with that alpha information, no blending takes place. 

If there is a clip rectangle set on the destination (set via \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a201a7363fdcfe07651a1298a3e4e1778}{SDL\_\-SetClipRect}) then this function will clip based on the intersection of the clip rectangle and the dstrect rectangle and the dstrect rectangle will be modified to represent the area actually filled. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
            int SDL_FillRect(SDL_Surface *dst, SDL_Rect *dstrect, Uint32 color);
\end{DoxyCode}
 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em surface}]IntPtr to \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___surface}{SDL\_\-Surface}\item[{\em rect}]IntPtr to \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___rect}{SDL\_\-Rect}\item[{\em color}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
This function returns 0 on success, or -\/1 on error. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a8c6c5785c9010c08364e8abcd34648a0}{SDL\_\-MapRGB}, \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_aadad00b884d9cab5dcfc16b887963bb3}{SDL\_\-MapRGBA}, \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_aec41f77b04d717457433acbecd7a257b}{SDL\_\-BlitSurface}, \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___rect}{SDL\_\-Rect}


\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_acc195af71a1137f48f929bf559d72bc0}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-Flip@{SDL\_\-Flip}}
\index{SDL\_\-Flip@{SDL\_\-Flip}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-Flip}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-Flip (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{IntPtr}]{ screen}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_acc195af71a1137f48f929bf559d72bc0}


Swaps screen buffers. 

On hardware that supports double-\/buffering, this function sets up a flip and returns. The hardware will wait for vertical retrace, and then swap video buffers before the next video surface blit or lock will return. On hardware that does not support double-\/buffering, this is equivalent to calling SDL\_\-UpdateRect(System.IntPtr, int, int, int, int)(screen, 0, 0, 0, 0) 

The SDL\_\-DOUBLEBUF flag must have been passed to \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a961f7efdc2a7ec3860e93140853092f7}{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode(int, int, int, int)} when setting the video mode for this function to perform hardware flipping.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em screen}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
This function returns 0 if successful, or -\/1 if there was an error. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a961f7efdc2a7ec3860e93140853092f7}{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode(int, int, int, int)}


\end{DoxySeeAlso}

Frees an SDL\_\-RWops structure allocated by \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_aa1fe24060926a8679b4a16201728a1e9}{SDL\_\-AllocRW}. 

\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a13c12ec9d6bfe668b50e13cb71ebd8ee}{SDL\_\-FreeRW} frees an SDL\_\-RWops structure previously allocated by \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_aa1fe24060926a8679b4a16201728a1e9}{SDL\_\-AllocRW}. Only use it on memory allocated by \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_aa1fe24060926a8679b4a16201728a1e9}{SDL\_\-AllocRW}. Any extra memory allocated during creation of the RWops is not freed by \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a13c12ec9d6bfe668b50e13cb71ebd8ee}{SDL\_\-FreeRW}; the programmer must be responsible for it. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em context}]\end{DoxyParams}

\begin{DoxyCode}
            #include "SDL_rwops.h"
            void dumb_example()
            {
                SDL_RWops *rw=SDL_AllocRW();
                if(rw==NULL) return;
                SDL_FreeRW(rw);
            }
\end{DoxyCode}


\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_aa1fe24060926a8679b4a16201728a1e9}{SDL\_\-AllocRW}


\end{DoxySeeAlso}

This function returns the current state of the application, which is a bitwise combination of SDL\_\-APPMOUSEFOCUS, SDL\_\-APPINPUTFOCUS, and SDL\_\-APPACTIVE. 

If SDL\_\-APPACTIVE is set, then the user is able to see your application, otherwise it has been iconified or disabled.

Gets the clipping rectangle for a surface. 

Gets the clipping rectangle for a surface. When this surface is the destination of a blit, only the area within the clip rectangle is drawn into. 

The rectangle pointed to by rect will be filled with the clipping rectangle of the surface.

Gets the color gamma lookup tables for the display. 

Gets the gamma translation lookup tables currently used by the display. Each table is an array of 256 short values. 

You must pass in valid pointers to arrays of 256 16-\/bit quantities. Any of the pointers may be NULL to ignore that channel.  

Not all display hardware is able to change gamma.  

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
int SDLCALL SDL_GetGammaRamp(Uint16 *red, Uint16 *green, Uint16 *blue)
\end{DoxyCode}
 

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
If the call succeeds, it will return 0. If the display driver or hardware does not support gamma translation, or otherwise fails, this function will return -\/1. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\item[{out int}]{ delay}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}

\label{_sdl_8cs_a8159db05cf68eb62d668e7c4bb8536b1}


Get keyboard repeat rate. 

Gets the keyboard repeat rate. delay specifies how long the key must be pressed before it begins repeating, it then repeats at the speed specified by interval. Both delay and interval are expressed in milliseconds. 

Setting delay to 0 disables key repeating completely. Good default values are SDL\_\-DEFAULT\_\-REPEAT\_\-DELAY and SDL\_\-DEFAULT\_\-REPEAT\_\-INTERVAL. p$>$Binds to C-\/function in SDL\_\-keyboard.h code$>$int SDL\_\-GetKeyRepeat(int delay, int interval); /code$>$


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em rate}]\item[{\em delay}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns 0 on success and -\/1 on failure.
\end{DoxyReturn}

Retrieve the current state of the mouse. 

The current button state is returned as a button bitmask, w hich can be tested using the SDL\_\-BUTTON(X) macros, and x and y are set to the current mouse cursor position. You can pass NULL for either x or y. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-mouse.h:

\end{DoxyReturn}

Retrieve the current state of the mouse. 

The current button state is returned as a button bitmask, which can be tested using the SDL\_\-BUTTON(X) macros, and x and y are set to the change in the mouse position since the last call to SDL\_\-GetRelativeMouseState or since event initialization. You can pass NULL for either x or y.

Get RGB values from a pixel in the specified pixel format. 

Get RGB component values from a pixel stored in the specified pixel format. 

This function uses the entire 8-\/bit \mbox{[}0..255\mbox{]} range when converting color components from pixel formats with less than 8-\/bits per RGB component (e.g., a completely white pixel in 16-\/bit RGB565 format would return \mbox{[}0xff, 0xff, 0xff\mbox{]} not \mbox{[}0xf8, 0xfc, 0xf8\mbox{]}). 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h:

\label{_sdl_8cs_a283f1dfcfccd35773f6f236a7c021033}


Get RGBA values from a pixel in the specified pixel format. 

Get RGBA component values from a pixel stored in the specified pixel format. 

This function uses the entire 8-\/bit \mbox{[}0..255\mbox{]} range when converting color components from pixel formats with less than 8-\/bits per RGB component (e.g., a completely white pixel in 16-\/bit RGB565 format would return \mbox{[}0xff, 0xff, 0xff\mbox{]} not \mbox{[}0xf8, 0xfc, 0xf8\mbox{]}). 

If the surface has no alpha component, the alpha will be returned as 0xff (100\% opaque). 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}

      , Uint8 *a)
\end{DoxyCode}

Gives you custom hooks into the window manager information. 

This function gives you custom hooks into the window manager information. It fills the structure pointed to by 'info' with custom information and returns 1 if the function is implemented. If it's not implemented, or the version member of the 'info' structure is invalid, it returns 0.

You typically use this function like this: SDL\_\-SysWMInfo info; SDL\_\-VERSION(\&info.version); if ( SDL\_\-GetWMInfo(\&info) ) \{ ... \}

Places the value of the SDL/OpenGL attribute attr into value. This is useful after a call to \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a961f7efdc2a7ec3860e93140853092f7}{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode(int, int, int, int)} to check whether your attributes have been \hyperlink{}{set} as you expected.

\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_af0c1ea0385d89fbb9decae290815f665}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-GL\_\-GetProcAddress@{SDL\_\-GL\_\-GetProcAddress}}
\index{SDL\_\-GL\_\-GetProcAddress@{SDL\_\-GL\_\-GetProcAddress}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-GL\_\-GetProcAddress}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static IntPtr SDL\_\-GL\_\-GetProcAddress (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{string}]{ proc}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_af0c1ea0385d89fbb9decae290815f665}


Get the address of a GL function. 

Returns the address of the GL function proc, or NULL if the function is not found. If the GL library is loaded at runtime, with SDL\_\-GL\_\-LoadLibrary, then all GL functions must be retrieved this way. Usually this is used to retrieve function pointers to OpenGL extensions. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
void *SDL_GL_GetProcAddress(const char* proc);
\end{DoxyCode}
  
\begin{DoxyCode}
            typedef void (*GL_ActiveTextureARB_Func)(unsigned int);
                        GL_ActiveTextureARB_Func glActiveTextureARB_ptr = 0;
                        int has_multitexture=1;
                        .
                        .
                        .
                        /* Get function pointer */
                        glActiveTextureARB_ptr=(GL_ActiveTextureARB_Func) 
      SDL_GL_GetProcAddress("glActiveTextureARB");

                        /* Check for a valid function ptr */
                        if(!glActiveTextureARB_ptr)
                                {
                        fprintf(stderr, "Multitexture Extensions not present.\n")
      ;
                        has_multitexture=0;
                }
                .
                .
                .
                .
                if(has_multitexture)
           {
                glActiveTextureARB_ptr(GL_TEXTURE0_ARB);
                .
                .
           }
                else
           {
                .
                .
           }
\end{DoxyCode}
 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em proc}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_abb5cc574ccf8709efaf0ad4ddff8a717}{SDL\_\-GL\_\-LoadLibrary}


\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns the address of the GL function proc, or NULL if the function is not found.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_abb5cc574ccf8709efaf0ad4ddff8a717}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-GL\_\-LoadLibrary@{SDL\_\-GL\_\-LoadLibrary}}
\index{SDL\_\-GL\_\-LoadLibrary@{SDL\_\-GL\_\-LoadLibrary}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-GL\_\-LoadLibrary}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-GL\_\-LoadLibrary (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{string}]{ path}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_abb5cc574ccf8709efaf0ad4ddff8a717}


Specify an OpenGL library. 

If you wish, you may load the OpenGL library at runtime, this must be done before \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a961f7efdc2a7ec3860e93140853092f7}{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode(int, int, int, int)} is called. The path of the GL library is passed to SDL\_\-GL\_\-LoadLibrary and it returns 0 on success, or -\/1 on an error. You must then use \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_af0c1ea0385d89fbb9decae290815f665}{SDL\_\-GL\_\-GetProcAddress} to retrieve function pointers to GL functions. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
int SDL_GL_LoadLibrary(const char *path);
\end{DoxyCode}
 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em path}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns 0 on success, or -\/1 on an error.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_af0c1ea0385d89fbb9decae290815f665}{SDL\_\-GL\_\-GetProcAddress}


\end{DoxySeeAlso}

Set a special SDL/OpenGL attribute. 

Sets the OpenGL attribute attr to value. The attributes you set don't take effect until after a call to \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a961f7efdc2a7ec3860e93140853092f7}{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode(int, int, int, int)}. You should use \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a9374dd6ba66cae1acd81cdb04fdb62db}{SDL\_\-GL\_\-GetAttribute} to check the values after a SDL\_\-SetVideoMode call.

\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-JoystickEventState@{SDL\_\-JoystickEventState}}
\index{SDL\_\-JoystickEventState@{SDL\_\-JoystickEventState}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-JoystickEventState}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-JoystickEventState (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{int}]{ state}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a4b5786d792bade406949c738f0290eca}


Enable/disable joystick event polling. 

This function is used to enable or disable joystick event processing. With joystick event processing disabled you will have to update joystick states with SDL\_\-JoystickUpdate and read the joystick information manually. state is either SDL\_\-QUERY, SDL\_\-ENABLE or SDL\_\-IGNORE. 

Note: Joystick event handling is preferred  

Binds to C-\/function in SDL\_\-joystick.h 
\begin{DoxyCode}
int SDL_JoystickEventState(int state)
\end{DoxyCode}


\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a1884e3601e7aa306d7b2e27884c16504}{SDL\_\-JoystickOpen}, \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_ab46ed3af900d20b62a7aa26570ecdff8}{SDL\_\-JoystickGetButton}, \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a37f3184ae17e4de28a75b8f2fdda592b}{SDL\_\-JoystickUpdate}, SDL\_\-JoyAxisEvent, SDL\_\-JoyBallEvent, SDL\_\-JoyButtonEvent, SDL\_\-JoyHatEvent


\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
If state is SDL\_\-QUERY then the current state is returned, otherwise the new processing state is returned. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_ab6c4b492ca0368f81c3aef8c49ebf21d}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-JoystickGetAxis@{SDL\_\-JoystickGetAxis}}
\index{SDL\_\-JoystickGetAxis@{SDL\_\-JoystickGetAxis}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-JoystickGetAxis}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static short SDL\_\-JoystickGetAxis (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{IntPtr}]{ joystick, }
\item[{int}]{ axis}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_ab6c4b492ca0368f81c3aef8c49ebf21d}


Get the current state of an axis. 

SDL\_\-JoystickGetAxis returns the current state of the given axis on the given joystick. 

On most modern joysticks the X axis is usually represented by axis 0 and the Y axis by axis 1. The value returned by SDL\_\-JoystickGetAxis is a signed integer (-\/32768 to 32768) representing the current position of the axis, it maybe necessary to impose certain tolerances on these values to account for jitter. It is worth noting that some joysticks use axes 2 and 3 for extra buttons. 

Binds to C-\/function in SDL\_\-joystick.h 
\begin{DoxyCode}
Sint16 SDL_JoystickGetAxis(SDL_Joystick *joystick, int axis);
\end{DoxyCode}



\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em joystick}]\item[{\em axis}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns a short representing the current position of the axis. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyCode}
            Sint16 x_move, y_move;
                        SDL_Joystick *joy1;
                        .
                        .
                        x_move=SDL_JoystickGetAxis(joy1, 0);
                        y_move=SDL_JoystickGetAxis(joy1, 1);
\end{DoxyCode}
 

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a80e04d0de1e40862a97c1851329bf360}{SDL\_\-JoystickNumAxes}


\end{DoxySeeAlso}

Get relative trackball motion. 

Get the ball axis change. 

Trackballs can only return relative motion since the last call to SDL\_\-JoystickGetBall, these motion deltas a placed into dx and dy.  

Binds to C-\/function in SDL\_\-joystick.h 
\begin{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxyCode}

Returns 0 on success or -\/1 on failure 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyCode}
            int delta_x, delta_y;
                        SDL_Joystick *joy;
                        .
                        .
                        .
                        SDL_JoystickUpdate();
                        if(SDL_JoystickGetBall(joy, 0, &amp;delta_x, &amp;delta_y
      )==-1)
                        printf("TrackBall Read Error!\n");
                        printf("Trackball Delta- X:%d, Y:%d\n", delta_x, delta_y)
      ;
\end{DoxyCode}

Open a joystick for use. 

Opens a joystick for use within SDL. The index refers to the N'th joystick in the system. A joystick must be opened before it game be used. 

Binds to C-\/function in SDL\_\-joystick.h 
\begin{DoxyCode}
\end{DoxyCode}



\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em device\_\-index}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns a IntPtr to a SDL\_\-Joystick structure on success. NULL on failure. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyCode}
            SDL_Joystick *joy;
            Check for joystick
                        if(SDL_NumJoysticks()>0)
                {
                        // Open joystick
                        joy=SDL_JoystickOpen(0);

                        if(joy)
                {
                        printf("Opened Joystick 0\n");
                        printf("Name: %s\n", SDL_JoystickName(0));
                        printf("Number of Axes: %d\n", SDL_JoystickNumAxes(joy));
      
                        printf("Number of Buttons: %d\n", SDL_JoystickNumButtons(
      joy));
                        printf("Number of Balls: %d\n", SDL_JoystickNumBalls(joy)
      );
                }
                else
                printf("Couldn't open Joystick 0\n");

                // Close if opened
                if(SDL_JoystickOpened(0))
                SDL_JoystickClose(joy);
           }
\end{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxyParamCaption}

\label{_sdl_8cs_a4b1642f748d1819ccb0d085a5c243c81}


This function loads a WAVE from the data source, automatically freeing that source if 'freesrc' is non-\/zero. For example, to load a WAVE file, you could do: SDL\_\-LoadWAV\_\-RW(SDL\_\-RWFromFile(\char`\"{}sample.wav\char`\"{}, \char`\"{}rb\char`\"{}), 1, ...);. 

If this function succeeds, it returns the given SDL\_\-AudioSpec, filled with the audio data format of the wave data, and sets 'audio\_\-buf' to a malloc()'d buffer containing the audio data, and sets 'audio\_\-len' to the length of that audio buffer, in bytes. You need to free the audio buffer with \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_aa59c06f2223e64f2b5f74b82625dd43f}{SDL\_\-FreeWAV()} when you are done with it. 

This function returns NULL and sets the SDL error message if the wave file cannot be opened, uses an unknown data format, or is corrupt. Currently raw and MS-\/ADPCM WAVE files are supported. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-audio.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
SDL_AudioSpec * SDL_LoadWAV_RW(SDL_RWops *src, int freesrc, SDL_AudioSpec *spec, 
      Uint8 **audio_buf, Uint32 *audio_len)
\end{DoxyCode}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}

\end{DoxyReturn}

Lock out the callback function. 

The lock manipulated by these functions protects the callback function. During a LockAudio period, you can be guaranteed that the callback function is not running. Do not call these from the callback function or you will cause deadlock. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-audio.h:

\begin{DoxyParamCaption}

\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_ad1c3562c62aaf55f95641f0bafab9e8f}


Lock a surface for directly access. 

SDL\_\-LockSurface sets up a surface for directly accessing the pixels. Between calls to SDL\_\-LockSurface and SDL\_\-UnlockSurface, you can write to and read from {\itshape surface.pixels\/}, using the pixel format stored in {\itshape surface.format\/}. Once you are done accessing the surface, you should use SDL\_\-UnlockSurface to release it. 

Not all surfaces require locking. If SDL\_\-MUSTLOCK(surface) evaluates to 0, then you can read and write to the surface at any time, and the pixel format of the surface will not change.  

No operating system or library calls should be made between lock/unlock pairs, as critical system locks may be held during this time.  

It should be noted, that since SDL 1.1.8 surface locks are recursive. This means that you can lock a surface multiple times, but each lock must have a match unlock.  code$>$ \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_ad1c3562c62aaf55f95641f0bafab9e8f}{SDL\_\-LockSurface( surface )}; /$\ast$ Surface is locked \hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_aef75e3a4590a542c940f024fa387031d}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-LockYUVOverlay@{SDL\_\-LockYUVOverlay}}
\index{SDL\_\-LockYUVOverlay@{SDL\_\-LockYUVOverlay}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}

\begin{DoxyParamCaption}

\item[{byte}]{ b}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}

\label{_sdl_8cs_a8c6c5785c9010c08364e8abcd34648a0}


Map a RGB color value to a pixel format. 

Maps the RGB color value to the specified pixel format and returns the pixel value as a 32-\/bit int. 

If the format has a palette (8-\/bit) the index of the closest matching color in the palette will be returned. 

If the specified pixel format has an alpha component it will be returned as all 1 bits (fully opaque). 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
extern DECLSPEC Uint32 SDLCALL SDL_MapRGB (SDL_PixelFormat *format, Uint8 r, Uint
      8 g, Uint8 b)
\end{DoxyCode}
 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em format}]IntPtr to \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___pixel_format}{SDL\_\-PixelFormat}\item[{\em r}]\item[{\em g}]\item[{\em b}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A pixel value best approximating the given RGB color value for a given pixel format. If the pixel format bpp (color depth) is less than 32-\/bpp then the unused upper bits of the return value can safely be ignored (e.g., with a 16-\/bpp format the return value can be assigned to a Uint16, and similarly a Uint8 for an 8-\/bpp format).
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_afff8f7111c4869f62dae87b04400b54d}{SDL\_\-GetRGB(int, IntPtr, out byte, out byte, out byte)}


\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_aadad00b884d9cab5dcfc16b887963bb3}


Map a RGBA color value to a pixel format. 

Maps the RGBA color value to the specified pixel format and returns the pixel value as a 32-\/bit int. 

If the format has a palette (8-\/bit) the index of the closest matching color in the palette will be returned. 

If the specified pixel format has no alpha component the alpha value will be ignored (as it will be in formats with a palette). 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
extern DECLSPEC Uint32 SDLCALL SDL_MapRGBA (SDL_PixelFormat *format, Uint8 r, Uin
      t8 g, Uint8 b, Uint8 a)
\end{DoxyCode}
 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em format}]\item[{\em r}]\item[{\em g}]\item[{\em b}]\item[{\em a}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A pixel value best approximating the given RGBA color value for a given pixel format. If the pixel format bpp (color depth) is less than 32-\/bpp then the unused upper bits of the return value can safely be ignored (e.g., with a 16-\/bpp format the return value can be assigned to a Uint16, and similarly a Uint8 for an 8-\/bpp format).
\end{DoxyReturn}

\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-MixAudio@{SDL\_\-MixAudio}}
\index{SDL\_\-MixAudio@{SDL\_\-MixAudio}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-MixAudio}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static void SDL\_\-MixAudio (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{IntPtr}]{ dst, }
\item[{IntPtr}]{ src, }
\item[{int}]{ len, }
\item[{int}]{ volume}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_affaed37dcb295519bdb4bce591c66797}


Mix audio data. 

This function takes two audio buffers of len bytes each of the playing audio format and mixes them, performing addition, volume adjustment, and overflow clipping. The volume ranges from 0 to SDL\_\-MIX\_\-MAXVOLUME and should be set to the maximum value for full audio volume. Note this does not change hardware volume. This is provided for convenience -\/-\/ you can mix your own audio data. 

Note: Do not use this function for mixing together more than two streams of sample data. The output from repeated application of this function may be distorted by clipping, because there is no accumulator with greater range than the input (not to mention this being an inefficient way of doing it). Use mixing functions from SDL\_\-mixer, OpenAL, or write your own mixer instead. 


\begin{DoxyCode}
            void SDL_MixAudio(Uint8 *dst, Uint8 *src, Uint32 len, int volume)
\end{DoxyCode}



\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}

Prototype for the new timer callback. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
The next timer interval. 
\end{DoxyReturn}


The callback function is passed the current timer interval and returns the next timer interval. If the returned value is the same as the one passed in, the periodic alarm continues, otherwise a new alarm is scheduled. If the callback returns 0, the periodic alarm is cancelled.

\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_ad374c9d61753113b30c8c4b96295ff3b}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-OpenAudio@{SDL\_\-OpenAudio}}
\index{SDL\_\-OpenAudio@{SDL\_\-OpenAudio}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-OpenAudio}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-OpenAudio (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{IntPtr}]{ desired, }
\item[{IntPtr}]{ obtained}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_ad374c9d61753113b30c8c4b96295ff3b}


Opens the audio device with the desired parameters. 

This function opens the audio device with the desired parameters, and returns 0 if successful, placing the actual hardware parameters in the structure pointed to by obtained. If obtained is NULL, the audio data passed to the callback function will be guaranteed to be in the requested format, and will be automatically converted to the hardware audio format if necessary. This function returns -\/1 if it failed to open the audio device, or couldn't set up the audio thread. 

To open the audio device a desired SDL\_\-AudioSpec must be created. 
\begin{DoxyCode}
            SDL_AudioSpec *desired;
            .
            .
            desired = malloc(sizeof(SDL_AudioSpec)); 
\end{DoxyCode}
 

You must then fill this structure with your desired audio specifications. 

desired-\/$>$freq The desired audio frequency in samples-\/per-\/second. 

desired-\/$>$format The desired audio format (see SDL\_\-AudioSpec) 

desired-\/$>$samples The desired size of the audio buffer in samples. This number should be a power of two, and may be adjusted by the audio driver to a value more suitable for the hardware. Good values seem to range between 512 and 8192 inclusive, depending on the application and CPU speed. Smaller values yield faster response time, but can lead to underflow if the application is doing heavy processing and cannot fill the audio buffer in time. A stereo sample consists of both right and left channels in LR ordering. Note that the number of samples is directly related to time by the following formula: ms = (samples$\ast$1000)/freq 

desired-\/$>$callback This should be set to a function that will be called when the audio device is ready for more data. It is passed a pointer to the audio buffer, and the length in bytes of the audio buffer. This function usually runs in a separate thread, and so you should protect data structures that it accesses by calling \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a228aa7a773a8820468022d53fed4ecd2}{SDL\_\-LockAudio} and \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a0a82eaee2425abf8428bca38acbbd8e6}{SDL\_\-UnlockAudio} in your code. The callback prototype is: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
            void callback(void *userdata, Uint8 *stream, int len);
\end{DoxyCode}
 

userdata is the pointer stored in userdata field of the SDL\_\-AudioSpec. stream is a pointer to the audio buffer you want to fill with information and len is the length of the audio buffer in bytes. 

desired-\/$>$userdata p$>$ This pointer is passed as the first parameter to the callback function. p$>$ SDL\_\-OpenAudio reads these fields from the desired SDL\_\-AudioSpec structure pass to the function and attempts to find an audio configuration matching your desired. As mentioned above, if the obtained parameter is NULL then SDL with convert from your desired audio settings to the hardware settings as it plays. p$>$If obtained is NULL then the desired SDL\_\-AudioSpec is your working specification, otherwise the obtained SDL\_\-AudioSpec becomes the working specification and the desirec specification can be deleted. The data in the working specification is used when building SDL\_\-AudioCVT's for converting loaded data to the hardware format. p$>$SDL\_\-OpenAudio calculates the size and silence fields for both the desired and obtained specifications. The size field stores the total size of the audio buffer in bytes, while the silence stores the value used to represent silence in the audio buffer.  

The audio device starts out playing silence when it's opened, and should be enabled for playing by calling \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a557320f482d1aa5bfe6121ee7cb7ad9f}{SDL\_\-PauseAudio}(0) when you are ready for your audio callback function to be called. Since the audio driver may modify the requested size of the audio buffer, you should allocate any local mixing buffers after you open the audio device. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-audio.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
int SDL_OpenAudio(SDL_AudioSpec *desired, SDL_AudioSpec *obtained);
\end{DoxyCode}



\begin{DoxyCode}
            /* Prototype of our callback function */
                        void my_audio_callback(void *userdata, Uint8 *stream, int
       len);

                        /* Open the audio device */
                        SDL_AudioSpec *desired, *obtained;
                        SDL_AudioSpec *hardware_spec;

                        /* Allocate a desired SDL_AudioSpec */
                        desired = malloc(sizeof(SDL_AudioSpec));

                        /* Allocate space for the obtained SDL_AudioSpec */
                        obtained = malloc(sizeof(SDL_AudioSpec));

                        /* 22050Hz - FM Radio quality */
                        desired-&gt;freq=22050;

                        /* 16-bit signed audio */
                        desired-&gt;format=AUDIO_S16LSB;

                        /* Mono */
                        desired-&gt;channels=0;

                /* Large audio buffer reduces risk of dropouts but 
                increases response time */
                        desired-&gt;samples=8192;

                        /* Our callback function */
                        desired-&gt;callback=my_audio_callback;

                        desired-&gt;userdata=NULL;

                        /* Open the audio device */
                        if ( SDL_OpenAudio(desired, obtained) &lt; 0 )
                {
                        fprintf(stderr, "Couldn't open audio: %s\n", SDL_GetError
      ());
                        exit(-1);
                }
                /* desired spec is no longer needed */
                free(desired);
                hardware_spec=obtained;
                .
                .
                /* Prepare callback for playing */
                .
                .
                .
                /* Start playing */
                SDL_PauseAudio(0);
\end{DoxyCode}
 /example$>$ 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em desired}]IntPtr to SDL\_\-AudioSpec\item[{\em obtained}]IntPtr to SDL\_\-AudioSpec\end{DoxyParams}

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\label{_sdl_8cs_a557320f482d1aa5bfe6121ee7cb7ad9f}


Pauses and unpauses the audio callback processing. 

This function pauses and unpauses the audio callback processing. It should be called with pause\_\-on=0 after opening the audio device to start playing sound. This is so you can safely initialize data for your callback function after opening the audio device. Silence will be written to the audio device during the pause.

\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_ac37ad33a4754eb016a62bf60e6401ca3}{

\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-PeepEvents}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-PeepEvents (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{\mbox{[}In, Out\mbox{]} SDL\_\-Event\mbox{[}$\,$\mbox{]}}]{ events, }
\item[{int}]{ numevents, }
\item[{int}]{ action, }
\item[{uint}]{ mask}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_ac37ad33a4754eb016a62bf60e6401ca3}


Checks the event queue for messages and optionally returns them. 

Checks the event queue for messages and optionally returns them. 

If action is SDL\_\-ADDEVENT, up to numevents events will be added to the back of the event queue. 

If action is SDL\_\-PEEKEVENT, up to numevents events at the front of the event queue, matching mask, will be returned and will not be removed from the queue. 

If action is SDL\_\-GETEVENT, up to numevents events at the front of the event queue, matching mask, will be returned and will be removed from the queue. 

The mask parameter is an bitwise OR of SDL\_\-EVENTMASK(event\_\-type), for all event types you are interested in.  

This function is thread-\/safe. 

Binds to C-\/function in SDL\_\-events.h 
\begin{DoxyCode}
            int SDL_PeepEvents(SDL_Event *events, int numevents, SDL_eventaction 
      action, Uint32 mask);
\end{DoxyCode}



\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
This function returns the number of events actually stored, or -\/1 if there was an error. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\end{DoxyParamCaption}

\label{_sdl_8cs_a85f90a4d8d6ae6e2ab13c9e286a9afd2}


Polls for currently pending events. 

Polls for currently pending events, and returns 1 if there are any pending events, or 0 if there are none available. 

If event is not NULL, the next event is removed from the queue and stored in that area. 

Binds to C-\/function in SDL\_\-events.h 
\begin{DoxyCode}
int SDL_PollEvent(SDL_Event *event);
\end{DoxyCode}
 


\begin{DoxyCode}
            SDL_Event event; /* Event structure */

                        .
                        .
                        .
                        /* Check for events */
                        while(SDL_PollEvent(&amp;event))
                {  /* Loop until there are no events left on the queue */
                        switch(event.type)
                                                 {  /* Process the appropiate eve
      nt type */
                        case SDL_KEYDOWN:  /* Handle a KEYDOWN event */         
                        printf("Oh! Key press\n");
                        break;
                        case SDL_MOUSEMOTION:
                        .
                        .
                        .
                        default: /* Report an unhandled event */
                        printf("I don't know what this event is!\n");
                }
           }
\end{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxyReturn}

\index{SDL\_\-PumpEvents@{SDL\_\-PumpEvents}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-PumpEvents}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static void SDL\_\-PumpEvents (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
{}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_aa58333f760b728cd8f56bbdbc8a6104e}


Pumps the event loop, gathering events from the input devices. 

Pumps the event loop, gathering events from the input devices. 

SDL\_\-PumpEvents gathers all the pending input information from devices and places it on the event queue. Without calls to SDL\_\-PumpEvents no events would ever be placed on the queue. Often calls the need for SDL\_\-PumpEvents is hidden from the user since \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a85f90a4d8d6ae6e2ab13c9e286a9afd2}{SDL\_\-PollEvent} and \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a6cf955d55444b337d368ea677e99b6f9}{SDL\_\-WaitEvent} implicitly call SDL\_\-PumpEvents. However, if you are not polling or waiting for events (e.g. you are filtering them), then you must call SDL\_\-PumpEvents to force an event queue update.  

Note: You can only call this function in the thread that set the video mode. 

Binds to C-\/function in SDL\_\-events.h 
\begin{DoxyCode}
            void SDL_PumpEvents(void);
\end{DoxyCode}


\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a85f90a4d8d6ae6e2ab13c9e286a9afd2}{SDL\_\-PollEvent}


\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_a521bf458cc5cfc65b822c2b5b8226646}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-PushEvent@{SDL\_\-PushEvent}}
\index{SDL\_\-PushEvent@{SDL\_\-PushEvent}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-PushEvent}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-PushEvent (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{out SDL\_\-Event}]{ evt}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a521bf458cc5cfc65b822c2b5b8226646}


Pushes an event onto the event queue. 

The event queue can actually be used as a two way communication channel. Not only can events be read from the queue, but the user can also push their own events onto it. event is a pointer to the event structure you wish to push onto the queue. 

Note: Pushing device input events onto the queue doesn't modify the state of the device within SDL. 

Binds to C-\/function in SDL\_\-events.h 
\begin{DoxyCode}
int SDL_PushEvent(SDL_Event *event)
\end{DoxyCode}
 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em evt}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns 0 on success or -\/1 if the event couldn't be pushed. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
SDL\_\-Event, \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a85f90a4d8d6ae6e2ab13c9e286a9afd2}{SDL\_\-PollEvent}, SDL\_\-PeepEvents(SDL\_\-Event\mbox{[}$\,$\mbox{]}, int, int, int)


\end{DoxySeeAlso}

{}

\label{_sdl_8cs_a3acfba2794297d8a0a6d5b047dbaa53c}


Shuts down SDL. 

{\bfseries SDL\_\-Quit} shuts down all SDL subsystems and frees the resources allocated to them. This should always be called before you exit. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
extern DECLSPEC void SDLCALL SDL_Quit(void)
\end{DoxyCode}

\item[{int}]{ size}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_ab5bf8b28e005615987c706138b89ff26}


Prepares a constant memory area for use with RWops. 

\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_ab5bf8b28e005615987c706138b89ff26}{SDL\_\-RWFromConstMem} sets up a RWops struct based on a memory area of a certain size. It assumes the memory area is not writable. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em mem}]\item[{\em size}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns a pointer to a new RWops struct, or NULL if it fails.
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyCode}
            char bitmap[] = {
                        66, 77, 86, 2, 0, 0, 0, 0 ...
                }
                 SDL_RWops *rw;
                 SDL_Surface *img;

                 rw = SDL_RWFromConstMem(bitmap, sizeof(bitmap));
                 img = SDL_LoadBMP_RW(rw, 1); // Automatically frees the RWops st
      ruct for us

                 //Do something with img...
\end{DoxyCode}


\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a5b1012f5444376abc443d022a9d8c547}{SDL\_\-RWFromMem(IntPtr, int)}


\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_a3c6da7942616b307b7fdf86e6402daf4}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-RWFromFP@{SDL\_\-RWFromFP}}
\index{SDL\_\-RWFromFP@{SDL\_\-RWFromFP}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-RWFromFP}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static IntPtr SDL\_\-RWFromFP (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{IntPtr}]{ fp, }
\item[{int}]{ autoclose}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a3c6da7942616b307b7fdf86e6402daf4}


SDL\_\-RWFromFP creates a new SDL\_\-RWops structure from a file pointer, opened with stdio. If autoclose is nonzero, the file will be automatically closed when the RWops structure is closed. 

This is not available under Win32, since files opened in an application on that platform cannot be used by a dynamically linked library. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em fp}]\item[{\em autoclose}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns pointer to a new RWops structure, or NULL if it fails.
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyCode}
            FILE *fp;
            SDL_RWops *rw;

            fp = fopen("myfile.dat", "rb");
            rw = SDL_RWFromFP(fp, 1);

            // Do things with rw...
            SDL_RWclose(rw); // Automatically does an fclose(fp)
\end{DoxyCode}


\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a5c5d2e26df99930f33d8b57c2a95874b}{SDL\_\-RWFromFile}


\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-SetAlpha@{SDL\_\-SetAlpha}}
\index{SDL\_\-SetAlpha@{SDL\_\-SetAlpha}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-SetAlpha}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-SetAlpha (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{IntPtr}]{ surface, }
\item[{int}]{ flag, }
\item[{byte}]{ alpha}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a77f6839de15f85b6c5afd9174894a41a}


Adjust the alpha properties of a surface. 

SDL\_\-SetAlpha is used for setting the per-\/surface alpha value and/or enabling and disabling alpha blending. 

The surface parameter specifies which surface whose alpha attributes you wish to adjust. flags is used to specify whether alpha blending should be used (SDL\_\-SRCALPHA) and whether the surface should use RLE acceleration for blitting (SDL\_\-RLEACCEL). flags can be an OR'd combination of these two options, one of these options or 0. If SDL\_\-SRCALPHA is not passed as a flag then all alpha information is ignored when blitting the surface. The alpha parameter is the per-\/surface alpha value; a surface need not have an alpha channel to use per-\/surface alpha and blitting can still be accelerated with SDL\_\-RLEACCEL. 

Note: The per-\/surface alpha value of 128 is considered a special case and is optimised, so it's much faster than other per-\/surface values. Alpha effects surface blitting in the following ways: \begin{TabularC}{2}
\hline
RGBA-\/$>$RGB with SDL\_\-SRCALPHA} &The source is alpha-\/blended with the destination, using the alpha channel. SDL\_\-SRCCOLORKEY and the per-\/surface alpha are ignored.  \\\cline{1-2}
RGBA-\/$>$RGB without SDL\_\-SRCALPHA} &The RGB data is copied from the source. The source alpha channel and the per-\/surface alpha value are ignored.  \\\cline{1-2}
RGB-\/$>$RGBA with SDL\_\-SRCALPHA} &The source is alpha-\/blended with the destination using the per-\/surface alpha value. If SDL\_\-SRCCOLORKEY is set, only the pixels not matching the colorkey value are copied. The alpha channel of the copied pixels is set to opaque.   \\\cline{1-2}
RGB-\/$>$RGBA without SDL\_\-SRCALPHA} &The RGB data is copied from the source and the alpha value of the copied pixels is set to opaque. If SDL\_\-SRCCOLORKEY is set, only the pixels not matching the colorkey value are copied.  \\\cline{1-2}
RGBA-\/$>$RGBA with SDL\_\-SRCALPHA} &The source is alpha-\/blended with the destination using the source alpha channel. The alpha channel in the destination surface is left untouched. SDL\_\-SRCCOLORKEY is ignored.   \\\cline{1-2}
RGBA-\/$>$RGBA without SDL\_\-SRCALPHA} &The RGBA data is copied to the destination surface. If SDL\_\-SRCCOLORKEY is set, only the pixels not matching the colorkey value are copied.   \\\cline{1-2}
RGB-\/$>$RGB with SDL\_\-SRCALPHA} &The source is alpha-\/blended with the destination using the per-\/surface alpha value. If SDL\_\-SRCCOLORKEY is set, only the pixels not matching the colorkey value are copied.   \\\cline{1-2}
RGB-\/$>$RGB without SDL\_\-SRCALPHA} &The RGB data is copied from the source. If SDL\_\-SRCCOLORKEY is set, only the pixels not matching the colorkey value are copied.   \\\cline{1-2}
\end{TabularC}


Note: Note that RGBA-\/$>$RGBA blits (with SDL\_\-SRCALPHA set) keep the alpha of the destination surface. This means that you cannot compose two arbitrary RGBA surfaces this way and get the result you would expect from \char`\"{}overlaying\char`\"{} them; the destination alpha will work as a mask. 

Also note that per-\/pixel and per-\/surface alpha cannot be combined; the per-\/pixel alpha is always used if available. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
int SDL_SetAlpha(SDL_Surface *surface, Uint32 flag, Uint8 alpha);
\end{DoxyCode}



\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em surface}]\item[{\em flag}]\item[{\em alpha}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
This function returns 0, or -\/1 if there was an error. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_aadad00b884d9cab5dcfc16b887963bb3}{SDL\_\-MapRGBA}


\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-SetClipRect@{SDL\_\-SetClipRect}}

\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-SetClipRect}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static void SDL\_\-SetClipRect (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}

\item[{ref {\bf SDL\_\-Rect}}]{ rect}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a201a7363fdcfe07651a1298a3e4e1778}


Sets the clipping rectangle for a surface. 

Sets the clipping rectangle for a surface. When this surface is the destination of a blit, only the area within the clip rectangle will be drawn into. 

The rectangle pointed to by rect will be clipped to the edges of the surface so that the clip rectangle for a surface can never fall outside the edges of the surface. 

If rect is NULL the clipping rectangle will be set to the full size of the surface. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
            void SDL_SetClipRect(SDL_Surface *surface, SDL_Rect *rect)
\end{DoxyCode}
