\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-SetColorKey}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-SetColorKey (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{IntPtr}]{ surface, }
\item[{int}]{ flag, }
\item[{int}]{ key}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a6143709fbf5b39f734e9de78cfa1d6c8}


Sets the color key (transparent pixel) in a blittable surface and RLE acceleration. 

Sets the color key (transparent pixel) in a blittable surface and enables or disables RLE blit acceleration. 

RLE acceleration can substantially speed up blitting of images with large horizontal runs of transparent pixels (i.e., pixels that match the key value). The key must be of the same pixel format as the surface, \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a8c6c5785c9010c08364e8abcd34648a0}{SDL\_\-MapRGB} is often useful for obtaining an acceptable value. 

If flag is SDL\_\-SRCCOLORKEY then key is the transparent pixel value in the source image of a blit. 

If flag is OR'd with SDL\_\-RLEACCEL then the surface will be draw using RLE acceleration when drawn with \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_aec41f77b04d717457433acbecd7a257b}{SDL\_\-BlitSurface}. The surface will actually be encoded for RLE acceleration the first time \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_aec41f77b04d717457433acbecd7a257b}{SDL\_\-BlitSurface} or \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a557565508a6c32f7bb4703f040a622c1}{SDL\_\-DisplayFormat} is called on the surface. 

If flag is 0, this function clears any current color key. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
int SDL_SetColorKey(SDL_Surface *surface, Uint32 flag, Uint32 key);
\end{DoxyCode}



\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em surface}]\item[{\em flag}]\item[{\em key}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
This function returns 0, or -\/1 if there was an error. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_aec41f77b04d717457433acbecd7a257b}{SDL\_\-BlitSurface}


\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-SetEventFilter@{SDL\_\-SetEventFilter}}
\index{SDL\_\-SetEventFilter@{SDL\_\-SetEventFilter}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-SetEventFilter}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static void SDL\_\-SetEventFilter (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{SDL\_\-EventFilter}]{ filter}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_afd1ab8f1891d71ad6544323050271d2d}


Sets up a filter to process all events before they are posted to the event queue. 

This function sets up a filter to process all events before they are posted to the event queue. This is a very powerful and flexible feature. The filter is prototyped as: 


\begin{DoxyCode}
typedef int (*SDL_EventFilter)(const SDL_Event *event);
\end{DoxyCode}
 

If the filter returns 1, then the event will be added to the internal queue. If it returns 0, then the event will be dropped from the queue. This allows selective filtering of dynamically.  

There is one caveat when dealing with the SDL\_\-QUITEVENT event type. The event filter is only called when the window manager desires to close the application window. If the event filter returns 1, then the window will be closed, otherwise the window will remain open if possible. If the quit event is generated by an interrupt signal, it will bypass the internal queue and be delivered to the application at the next event poll. 

Note: Events pushed onto the queue with \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a521bf458cc5cfc65b822c2b5b8226646}{SDL\_\-PushEvent} or SDL\_\-PeepEvents(SDL\_\-Event\mbox{[}$\,$\mbox{]}, int, int, int) do not get passed through the event filter. 

Note: Be Careful! The event filter function may run in a different thread so be careful what you do within it. 

Binds to C-\/function in SDL\_\-events.h 
\begin{DoxyCode}
void SDL_SetEventFilter(SDL_EventFilter filter);
\end{DoxyCode}



\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em filter}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
SDL\_\-Event, \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_aba4dab0b2d671d9f083744794ba77f2d}{SDL\_\-GetEventFilter}, \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a521bf458cc5cfc65b822c2b5b8226646}{SDL\_\-PushEvent}


\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_aec2c6c149b3567ffb29ff86bc202b43f}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-SetGamma@{SDL\_\-SetGamma}}

\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-SetGamma}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-SetGamma (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{float}]{ red, }
\item[{float}]{ green, }
\item[{float}]{ blue}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_aec2c6c149b3567ffb29ff86bc202b43f}


Set the gamma correction for each of the color channels. 

Sets the \char`\"{}gamma function\char`\"{} for the display of each color component. Gamma controls the brightness/contrast of colors displayed on the screen. A gamma value of 1.0 is identity (i.e., no adjustment is made).  

This function adjusts the gamma based on the \char`\"{}gamma function\char`\"{} parameter, you can directly specify lookup tables for gamma adjustment with SDL\_\-SetGammaRamp. 

Not all display hardware is able to change gamma. 

The gamma values range (approximately) between 0.1 and 10.0. 

If this function isn't supported directly by the hardware, it will be emulated using gamma ramps, if available. If successful, this function returns 0, otherwise it returns -\/1. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
extern DECLSPEC int SDLCALL SDL_SetGamma(float red, float green, float blue)
\end{DoxyCode}
 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em blue}]\item[{\em green}]\item[{\em red}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
If successful, this function returns 0, otherwise it returns -\/1. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-SetGammaRamp}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-SetGammaRamp (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{\mbox{[}In, Out\mbox{]} short\mbox{[}$\,$\mbox{]}}]{ red, }
\item[{\mbox{[}In, Out\mbox{]} short\mbox{[}$\,$\mbox{]}}]{ green, }
\item[{\mbox{[}In, Out\mbox{]} short\mbox{[}$\,$\mbox{]}}]{ blue}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_add53fba5948db676ea3988e8d8b040cf}


Set the gamma translation table for the red, green, and blue channels of the video hardware. 

Each table is an array of 256 16-\/bit quantities, representing a mapping between the input and output for that channel. The input is the index into the array, and the output is the 16-\/bit gamma value at that index, scaled to the output color precision. You may pass NULL for any of the channels to leave it unchanged.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
If the call succeeds, it will return 0. If the display driver or hardware does not support gamma translation, or otherwise fails, this function will return -\/1. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em blue}]\item[{\em green}]\item[{\em red}]\end{DoxyParams}

\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_a43f6e27a3a67800dd7c252305fe79839}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-SetTimer@{SDL\_\-SetTimer}}
\index{SDL\_\-SetTimer@{SDL\_\-SetTimer}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-SetTimer}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-SetTimer (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{int}]{ interval, }
\item[{SDL\_\-TimerCallback}]{ callback}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a43f6e27a3a67800dd7c252305fe79839}


Set a callback to run after the specified number of milliseconds has elapsed. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em interval}]The timer interval. \item[{\em callback}]The callback to run. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
The next timer interval. 
\end{DoxyReturn}


The callback function is passed the current timer interval and returns the next timer interval. If the returned value is the same as the one passed in, the periodic alarm continues, otherwise a new alarm is scheduled. 

To cancel a currently running timer, call {\ttfamily Sdl.SDL\_\-SetTimer(0, null);} 

The timer callback function may run in a different thread than your main constant, and so shouldn't call any functions from within itself. 

The maximum resolution of this timer is 10 ms, which means that if you request a 16 ms timer, your callback will run approximately 20 ms later on an unloaded system. If you wanted to set a flag signaling a frame update at 30 frames per second (every 33 ms), you might set a timer for 30 ms. 

If you use this function, you need to pass SDL\_\-INIT\_\-TIMER to SDL\_\-Init(int). 

This function is kept for compatibility but has been superseded by the new timer functions \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a0847fd552fc17aa314f866ac16db60df}{SDL\_\-AddTimer(int, SDL\_\-NewTimerCallback)} and \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a135aaf0e0425b1dcf1904b966509c3c0}{SDL\_\-RemoveTimer} which support multiple timers. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-timer.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
extern DECLSPEC int SDLCALL SDL_SetTimer(Uint32 interval, 
                SDL_TimerCallback callback)
\end{DoxyCode}
 

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a0847fd552fc17aa314f866ac16db60df}{SDL\_\-AddTimer(int, SDL\_\-NewTimerCallback)}, \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a43a7c7ef24b53b00cb058b4e7d446d75}{SDL\_\-TimerCallback}


\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_a7e9d2d16dfb1cdd312f1d0b45f989dcc}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-SetTimer@{SDL\_\-SetTimer}}
\index{SDL\_\-SetTimer@{SDL\_\-SetTimer}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-SetTimer}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-SetTimer (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{uint}]{ interval, }
\item[{SDL\_\-TimerCallback}]{ callback}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a7e9d2d16dfb1cdd312f1d0b45f989dcc}

\item[{\em interval}]The timer interval. \item[{\em callback}]The callback to run. \end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
The next timer interval. 
\end{DoxyReturn}


The callback function is passed the current timer interval and returns the next timer interval. If the returned value is the same as the one passed in, the periodic alarm continues, otherwise a new alarm is scheduled. 

To cancel a currently running timer, call {\ttfamily Sdl.SDL\_\-SetTimer(0, null);} 

The timer callback function may run in a different thread than your main constant, and so shouldn't call any functions from within itself. 

The maximum resolution of this timer is 10 ms, which means that if you request a 16 ms timer, your callback will run approximately 20 ms later on an unloaded system. If you wanted to set a flag signaling a frame update at 30 frames per second (every 33 ms), you might set a timer for 30 ms. 

If you use this function, you need to pass SDL\_\-INIT\_\-TIMER to SDL\_\-Init(int). 

This function is kept for compatibility but has been superseded by the new timer functions \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a0847fd552fc17aa314f866ac16db60df}{SDL\_\-AddTimer(int, SDL\_\-NewTimerCallback)} and \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a135aaf0e0425b1dcf1904b966509c3c0}{SDL\_\-RemoveTimer} which support multiple timers.

  \begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a43a7c7ef24b53b00cb058b4e7d446d75}{SDL\_\-TimerCallback}


\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_a9f7878de4f7e109ea2485a4865d81afd}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-SetVideoMode@{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode}}
\index{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode@{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static IntPtr SDL\_\-SetVideoMode (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{int}]{ width, }
\item[{int}]{ height, }
\item[{int}]{ bpp, }
\item[{uint}]{ flags}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a9f7878de4f7e109ea2485a4865d81afd}


Set up a video mode with the specified width, height and bits-\/per-\/pixel. 

If 'bpp' is 0, it is treated as the current display bits per pixel. 

The flags parameter is the same as the flags field of the \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___surface}{SDL\_\-Surface} structure. OR'd combinations of the following values are valid.  \begin{TabularC}{2}
\hline
Flag} &Description  \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-SWSURFACE} &Create the video surface in system memory.  \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-HWSURFACE} &Create the video surface in video memory ,if possible, and you may have to call \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_ad1c3562c62aaf55f95641f0bafab9e8f}{SDL\_\-LockSurface()} in order to access the raw framebuffer. Otherwise, the video surface will be created in system memory.  \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-ASYNCBLIT} &Enables the use of asynchronous updates of the display surface, but you must always lock before accessing pixels. SDL will wait for updates to complete before returning from the lock. This will usually slow down blitting on single CPU machines, but may provide a speed increase on SMP systems.  \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-ANYFORMAT} &Normally, if a video surface of the requested bits-\/per-\/pixel (bpp) is not available, SDL will emulate one with a shadow surface. Passing SDL\_\-ANYFORMAT prevents this and causes SDL to use the video surface, regardless of its pixel depth.  \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-HWPALETTE} &Give SDL exclusive palette access. Without this flag you may not always get the the colors you request with \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a7d863c2bb7590dba1b9eb040d44449e7}{SDL\_\-SetColors} or \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_afe8acab3b160f7859c903cec5fbb4f86}{SDL\_\-SetPalette}. You should look at the video surface structure to determine the actual palette. If SDL cannot guarantee that the colors you request can be set, i.e. if the colormap is shared, then the video surface may be created under emulation in system memory, overriding the SDL\_\-HWSURFACE flag.   \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-DOUBLEBUF} &Enable hardware double buffering; only valid with SDL\_\-HWSURFACE. Calling \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_acc195af71a1137f48f929bf559d72bc0}{SDL\_\-Flip} will flip the buffers and update the screen. All drawing will take place on the surface that is not displayed at the moment. If double buffering could not be enabled then SDL\_\-Flip will just perform a SDL\_\-UpdateRect(System.IntPtr, int, int, int, int) on the entire screen. This is usually slower than the normal single-\/buffering scheme, but prevents \char`\"{}tearing\char`\"{} artifacts caused by modifying video memory while the monitor is refreshing. It should only be used by applications that redraw the entire screen on every update.  \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-FULLSCREEN} &SDL will attempt to use a fullscreen mode. If a hardware resolution change is not possible (for whatever reason), the next higher resolution will be used and the display window centered on a black background. The default is to create a windowed mode if the current graphics system has a window manager. If the SDL library is able to set a fullscreen video mode, this flag will be set in the surface that is returned.  \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-OPENGL} &Create an OpenGL rendering context. You should have previously set OpenGL video attributes with \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a9d12980991f938865faa9cc236d88825}{SDL\_\-GL\_\-SetAttribute}.   \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-OPENGLBLIT} &Create an OpenGL rendering context, like above, but allow normal blitting operations. The screen (2D) surface may have an alpha channel, and \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a7a553064b9c7c9be654714fa618d67db}{SDL\_\-UpdateRects} must be used for updating changes to the screen surface. NOTE: This option is kept for compatibility only, and is not recommended for new code.   \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-RESIZABLE} &Create a resizable window. When the window is resized by the user a SDL\_\-VIDEORESIZE event is generated and SDL\_\-SetVideoMode can be called again with the new size.   \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-NOFRAME} &If possible, SDL\_\-NOFRAME causes SDL to create a window with no title bar or frame decoration. Fullscreen modes automatically have this flag set.   \\\cline{1-2}
\end{TabularC}


If you rely on functionality provided by certain video flags, check the flags of the returned surface to make sure that functionality is available. SDL will fall back to reduced functionality if the exact flags you wanted are not available. 

Whatever flags SDL\_\-SetVideoMode could satisfy are set in the flags member of the returned surface. 

The bpp parameter is the number of bits per pixel, so a bpp of 24 uses the packed representation of 3 bytes/pixel. For the more common 4 bytes/pixel mode, use a bpp of 32. Somewhat oddly, both 15 and 16 will request a 2 bytes/pixel mode, but different pixel formats.  

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
extern DECLSPEC SDL_Surface * SDLCALL SDL_SetVideoMode
            (int width, int height, int bpp, Uint32 flags);
\end{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\end{DoxyReturn}
\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_a961f7efdc2a7ec3860e93140853092f7}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-SetVideoMode@{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode}}
\index{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode@{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static IntPtr SDL\_\-SetVideoMode (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{int}]{ width, }
\item[{int}]{ height, }
\item[{int}]{ bpp, }
\item[{int}]{ flags}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a961f7efdc2a7ec3860e93140853092f7}


Set up a video mode with the specified width, height and bits-\/per-\/pixel. 

If 'bpp' is 0, it is treated as the current display bits per pixel. 

The flags parameter is the same as the flags field of the \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___surface}{SDL\_\-Surface} structure. OR'd combinations of the following values are valid.  \begin{TabularC}{2}
\hline
Flag} &Description  \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-SWSURFACE} &Create the video surface in system memory.  \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-HWSURFACE} &Create the video surface in video memory ,if possible, and you may have to call \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_ad1c3562c62aaf55f95641f0bafab9e8f}{SDL\_\-LockSurface()} in order to access the raw framebuffer. Otherwise, the video surface will be created in system memory.  \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-ASYNCBLIT} &Enables the use of asynchronous updates of the display surface, but you must always lock before accessing pixels. SDL will wait for updates to complete before returning from the lock. This will usually slow down blitting on single CPU machines, but may provide a speed increase on SMP systems.  \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-ANYFORMAT} &Normally, if a video surface of the requested bits-\/per-\/pixel (bpp) is not available, SDL will emulate one with a shadow surface. Passing SDL\_\-ANYFORMAT prevents this and causes SDL to use the video surface, regardless of its pixel depth.  \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-HWPALETTE} &Give SDL exclusive palette access. Without this flag you may not always get the the colors you request with \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a7d863c2bb7590dba1b9eb040d44449e7}{SDL\_\-SetColors} or \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_afe8acab3b160f7859c903cec5fbb4f86}{SDL\_\-SetPalette}. You should look at the video surface structure to determine the actual palette. If SDL cannot guarantee that the colors you request can be set, i.e. if the colormap is shared, then the video surface may be created under emulation in system memory, overriding the SDL\_\-HWSURFACE flag.   \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-DOUBLEBUF} &Enable hardware double buffering; only valid with SDL\_\-HWSURFACE. Calling \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_acc195af71a1137f48f929bf559d72bc0}{SDL\_\-Flip} will flip the buffers and update the screen. All drawing will take place on the surface that is not displayed at the moment. If double buffering could not be enabled then SDL\_\-Flip will just perform a SDL\_\-UpdateRect(System.IntPtr, int, int, int, int) on the entire screen. This is usually slower than the normal single-\/buffering scheme, but prevents \char`\"{}tearing\char`\"{} artifacts caused by modifying video memory while the monitor is refreshing. It should only be used by applications that redraw the entire screen on every update.  \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-FULLSCREEN} &SDL will attempt to use a fullscreen mode. If a hardware resolution change is not possible (for whatever reason), the next higher resolution will be used and the display window centered on a black background. The default is to create a windowed mode if the current graphics system has a window manager. If the SDL library is able to set a fullscreen video mode, this flag will be set in the surface that is returned.  \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-OPENGL} &Create an OpenGL rendering context. You should have previously set OpenGL video attributes with \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a9d12980991f938865faa9cc236d88825}{SDL\_\-GL\_\-SetAttribute}.   \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-OPENGLBLIT} &Create an OpenGL rendering context, like above, but allow normal blitting operations. The screen (2D) surface may have an alpha channel, and \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a7a553064b9c7c9be654714fa618d67db}{SDL\_\-UpdateRects} must be used for updating changes to the screen surface. NOTE: This option is kept for compatibility only, and is not recommended for new code.   \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-RESIZABLE} &Create a resizable window. When the window is resized by the user a SDL\_\-VIDEORESIZE event is generated and SDL\_\-SetVideoMode can be called again with the new size.   \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-NOFRAME} &If possible, SDL\_\-NOFRAME causes SDL to create a window with no title bar or frame decoration. Fullscreen modes automatically have this flag set.   \\\cline{1-2}
\end{TabularC}


If you rely on functionality provided by certain video flags, check the flags of the returned surface to make sure that functionality is available. SDL will fall back to reduced functionality if the exact flags you wanted are not available. 

Whatever flags SDL\_\-SetVideoMode could satisfy are set in the flags member of the returned surface. 

The bpp parameter is the number of bits per pixel, so a bpp of 24 uses the packed representation of 3 bytes/pixel. For the more common 4 bytes/pixel mode, use a bpp of 32. Somewhat oddly, both 15 and 16 will request a 2 bytes/pixel mode, but different pixel formats.  

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}

            (int width, int height, int bpp, Uint32 flags);
\end{DoxyCode}

\label{_sdl_8cs_a4e85211428ccac72ba71d06b2391ab06}


Toggle whether or not the cursor is shown on the screen. 

Toggle whether or not the cursor is shown on the screen. Passing SDL\_\-ENABLE displays the cursor and passing SDL\_\-DISABLE hides it. The current state of the mouse cursor can be queried by passing SDL\_\-QUERY, either SDL\_\-DISABLE or SDL\_\-ENABLE will be returned. 

The cursor starts off displayed, but can be turned off.  

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-mouse.h:

Unlocks a previously locked surface. 

Surfaces that were previously locked using \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_afae9570bf3fb2b26f7403cb1fc4f1353}{SDL\_\-LockSurface} must be unlocked with SDL\_\-UnlockSurface. Surfaces should be unlocked as soon as possible. 

It should be noted that since 1.1.8, surface locks are recursive. See \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_afae9570bf3fb2b26f7403cb1fc4f1353}{SDL\_\-LockSurface}.

Makes sure the given area is updated on the given screen. 

The rectangle must be confined within the screen boundaries (no clipping is done).  

If 'x', 'y', 'w' and 'h' are all 0, SDL\_\-UpdateRect will update the entire screen. 

These functions should not be called while 'screen' is \hyperlink{}{locked}.

\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-UpdateRects@{SDL\_\-UpdateRects}}
\index{SDL\_\-UpdateRects@{SDL\_\-UpdateRects}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-UpdateRects}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static void SDL\_\-UpdateRects (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{IntPtr}]{ screen, }
\item[{int}]{ numrects, }
\item[{\mbox{[}In, Out\mbox{]} {\bf SDL\_\-Rect}\mbox{[}$\,$\mbox{]}}]{ rects}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a7a553064b9c7c9be654714fa618d67db}


Makes sure the given list of rectangles is updated on the given screen. 

The rectangles must all be confined within the screen boundaries (no clipping is done). 

This function should not be called while screen is locked.  

Note: It is adviced to call this function only once per frame, since each call has some processing overhead. This is no restriction since you can pass any number of rectangles each time.  

The rectangles are not automatically merged or checked for overlap. In general, the programmer can use his knowledge about his particular rectangles to merge them in an efficient way, to avoid overdraw. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
extern DECLSPEC void SDLCALL SDL_UpdateRects (SDL_Surface *screen, int numrects, 
      SDL_Rect *rects)
\end{DoxyCode}

\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_ac022f5f4d029ec3d89f6257b8f716951}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-VideoModeOK@{SDL\_\-VideoModeOK}}
\index{SDL\_\-VideoModeOK@{SDL\_\-VideoModeOK}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-VideoModeOK}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-VideoModeOK (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{int}]{ width, }
\item[{int}]{ height, }
\item[{int}]{ bpp, }
\item[{int}]{ flags}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_ac022f5f4d029ec3d89f6257b8f716951}


Check to see if a particular video mode is supported. 

SDL\_\-VideoModeOK returns 0 if the requested mode is not supported under any bit depth, or returns the bits-\/per-\/pixel of the closest available mode with the given width, height and requested \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___surface}{SDL\_\-Surface} flags. See \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a961f7efdc2a7ec3860e93140853092f7}{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode(int, int, int, int)}. 

The bits-\/per-\/pixel value returned is only a suggested mode. You can usually request and bpp you want when setting the video mode and SDL will emulate that color depth with a shadow video surface.  

The arguments to \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_ac022f5f4d029ec3d89f6257b8f716951}{SDL\_\-VideoModeOK()} are the same ones you would pass to \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a961f7efdc2a7ec3860e93140853092f7}{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode(int, int, int, int)}  

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
extern DECLSPEC int SDLCALL SDL_VideoModeOK(int width, int height, int bpp, Uint3

\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-VideoModeOK}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-VideoModeOK (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}

\item[{int}]{ height, }
\item[{int}]{ bpp, }
\item[{uint}]{ flags}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a7af0f2e30f654a9e5f260d561fe09ef8}


Check to see if a particular video mode is supported. 

SDL\_\-VideoModeOK returns 0 if the requested mode is not supported under any bit depth, or returns the bits-\/per-\/pixel of the closest available mode with the given width, height and requested \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___surface}{SDL\_\-Surface} flags. See \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a961f7efdc2a7ec3860e93140853092f7}{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode(int, int, int, int)}. 

The bits-\/per-\/pixel value returned is only a suggested mode. You can usually request and bpp you want when setting the video mode and SDL will emulate that color depth with a shadow video surface.  

The arguments to \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_ac022f5f4d029ec3d89f6257b8f716951}{SDL\_\-VideoModeOK()} are the same ones you would pass to \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a961f7efdc2a7ec3860e93140853092f7}{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode(int, int, int, int)}  

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
extern DECLSPEC int SDLCALL SDL_VideoModeOK(int width, int height, int bpp, Uint3
      2 flags)
\end{DoxyCode}
 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em width}]Width of mode\item[{\em height}]Height of mode\item[{\em bpp}]bit depth of Mode\item[{\em flags}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}

\end{DoxyReturn}

Waits indefinitely for the next available event. 

Waits indefinitely for the next available event, returning 1, or 0 if there was an error while waiting for events. 

If 'event' is not NULL, the next event is removed from the queue and stored in that area.

\label{_sdl_8cs_ad70ae8fd84dc3156a6d670ae8532da28}


Grabs mouse and keyboard input. 

Grabbing means that the mouse is confined to the application window, and nearly all keyboard input is passed directly to the application, and not interpreted by a window manager, if any. 

When mode is SDL\_\-GRAB\_\-QUERY the grab mode is not changed, but the current grab mode is returned.

\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-WM\_\-SetIcon}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static void SDL\_\-WM\_\-SetIcon (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{IntPtr}]{ icon, }
\item[{byte\mbox{[}$\,$\mbox{]}}]{ mask}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a4812354ffe2ef55699b0190e6a41ebf3}


Sets the icon for the display window. 

Sets the icon for the display window. Win32 icons must be 32x32. 

This function must be called before the first call to \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a961f7efdc2a7ec3860e93140853092f7}{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode(int, int, int, int)}. 

The mask is a bitmask that describes the shape of the icon. If mask is NULL, then the shape is determined by the colorkey of icon, if any, or makes the icon rectangular (no transparency) otherwise. 

If mask is non-\/NULL, it points to a bitmap with bits set where the corresponding pixel should be visible. The format of the bitmap is as follows: Scanlines come in the usual top-\/down order. Each scanline consists of (width / 8) bytes, rounded up. The most significant bit of each byte represents the leftmost pixel. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
void SDL_WM_SetIcon(SDL_Surface *icon, Uint8 *mask);
\end{DoxyCode}



\begin{DoxyCode}
SDL_WM_SetIcon(SDL_LoadBMP("icon.bmp"), NULL);
\end{DoxyCode}



\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em icon}]Pointer to an \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___surface}{SDL\_\-Surface}\item[{\em mask}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a961f7efdc2a7ec3860e93140853092f7}{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode(int, int, int, int)}, \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a166b37121b66298e3f76a4fd8a4890fc}{SDL\_\-WM\_\-SetCaption}


\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_ab0e1ad78990e0c3ec5522d9ba29aca74}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!SDL\_\-WM\_\-ToggleFullScreen@{SDL\_\-WM\_\-ToggleFullScreen}}
\index{SDL\_\-WM\_\-ToggleFullScreen@{SDL\_\-WM\_\-ToggleFullScreen}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{SDL\_\-WM\_\-ToggleFullScreen}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}static int SDL\_\-WM\_\-ToggleFullScreen (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{IntPtr}]{ surface}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_ab0e1ad78990e0c3ec5522d9ba29aca74}


Toggle fullscreen mode without changing the contents of the screen. 

If the display surface does not require locking before accessing the pixel information, then the memory pointers will not change. p$>$If this function was able to toggle fullscreen mode (change from running in a window to fullscreen, or vice-\/versa), it will return 1. If it is not implemented, or fails, it returns 0. 

The next call to \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a961f7efdc2a7ec3860e93140853092f7}{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode()} will set the mode fullscreen attribute based on the flags parameter -\/ if SDL\_\-FULLSCREEN is not set, then the display will be windowed by default where supported. 

This is currently only implemented in the X11 video driver. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
int SDL_WM_ToggleFullScreen(SDL_Surface *surface);
\end{DoxyCode}



\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
\item[{\em surface}]\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns 0 on failure or 1 on success.
\end{DoxyReturn}

\subsubsection[{colors}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}{\bf SDL\_\-Color} {\bf colors}}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_aece5a7af4770c985f1b8cc20246f5b28}
\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_a36910ddc19d1bf237b12507db74f71a2}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!fmt@{fmt}}
\index{fmt@{fmt}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{fmt}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}{\bf fmt} = surface.format}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a36910ddc19d1bf237b12507db74f71a2}


Stores surface format information. 

A \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___pixel_format}{SDL\_\-PixelFormat} describes the format of the pixel data stored at the pixels field of a \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___surface}{SDL\_\-Surface}. Every surface stores a \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___pixel_format}{SDL\_\-PixelFormat} in the format field. 

If you wish to do pixel level modifications on a surface, then understanding how SDL stores its color information is essential.  

8-\/bit pixel formats are the easiest to understand. Since its an 8-\/bit format, we have 8 BitsPerPixel and 1 BytesPerPixel. Since BytesPerPixel is 1, all pixels are represented by a Uint8 which contains an index into palette.colors. So, to determine the color of a pixel in a 8-\/bit surface: we read the color index from surface.pixels and we use that index to read the \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___color}{SDL\_\-Color} structure from surface.format.palette.colors. Like so:  


\begin{DoxyCode}
                        SDL_Surface *surface;
                        SDL_PixelFormat *fmt;
                        SDL_Color *color;
                        Uint8 index;

                        .
                        .

                        /* Create surface */
                        .
                        .
                        fmt=surface.format;

                        /* Check the bitdepth of the surface */
                        if(fmt.BitsPerPixel!=8)
                {
                        fprintf(stderr, "Not an 8-bit surface.\n");
                        return(-1);
                }

                /* Lock the surface */
                SDL_LockSurface(surface);

                /* Get the topleft pixel */
                index=*(Uint8 *)surface.pixels;
                color=fmt.palette.colors[index];

                /* Unlock the surface */
                SDL_UnlockSurface(surface);
                printf("Pixel Color- Red: %d, Green: %d, Blue: %d. Index: %d\n",
                color.r, color.g, color.b, index);
                .
                .
\end{DoxyCode}
  

Pixel formats above 8-\/bit are an entirely different experience. They are considered to be \char`\"{}TrueColor\char`\"{} formats and the color information is stored in the pixels themselves, not in a palette. The mask, shift and loss fields tell us how the color information is encoded. The mask fields allow us to isolate each color component, the shift fields tell us the number of bits to the right of each component in the pixel value and the loss fields tell us the number of bits lost from each component when packing 8-\/bit color component in a pixel. 

code$>$ /$\ast$ Extracting color components from a 32-\/bit color value \hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_aed8345802a260785e5cc4fead969a627}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!given@{given}}
\index{given@{given}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{given}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}$<$/code $>$$<$/example $>$$<$ paramname=\char`\"{}surface\char`\"{}$>$$<$/param $>$$<$ paramname=\char`\"{}colors\char`\"{}$>$$<$/param $>$$<$ paramname=\char`\"{}firstcolor\char`\"{}$>$$<$/param $>$$<$ paramname=\char`\"{}flags\char`\"{}$>$$<$/param $>$$<$ paramname=\char`\"{}ncolors\char`\"{}$>$$<$/param $>$$<$ returns $>$ If {\bf surface} is not a palettized this function does returning If all of the {\bf colors} were set as passed to it will {\bf return} If not all the color entries were set exactly as {\bf given}}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_aed8345802a260785e5cc4fead969a627}
\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_ab9cc005962591e6805dd39a2fda8a836}{

\hypertarget{_sdl_8cs_a968bba55c7ad32b326939fefd1bbb017}{
\index{Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}!screen@{screen}}
\index{screen@{screen}!Sdl.cs@{Sdl.cs}}
\subsubsection[{screen}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}{\bf SDL\_\-Surface} $\ast$ {\bf screen} = SDL\_\-SetVideoMode(640, 480, 8, SDL\_\-HWPALETTE)}}
\label{_sdl_8cs_a968bba55c7ad32b326939fefd1bbb017}


Sets a portion of the colormap for the given 8-\/bit surface. 

Sets the colors in the palette of an 8-\/bit surface.

When surface is the surface associated with the current display, the display colormap will be updated with the requested colors. If SDL\_\-HWPALETTE was set in \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a961f7efdc2a7ec3860e93140853092f7}{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode(int, int, int, int)} flags, SDL\_\-SetColors will always return 1, and the palette is guaranteed to be set the way you desire, even if the window colormap has to be warped or run under emulation.

The color components of a \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___color}{SDL\_\-Color} structure are 8-\/bits in size, giving you a total of 256$^\wedge$3 =16777216 colors. 

Palettized (8-\/bit) screen surfaces with the SDL\_\-HWPALETTE flag have two palettes, a logical palette that is used for mapping blits to/from the surface and a physical palette (that determines how the hardware will map the colors to the display). SDL\_\-SetColors modifies both palettes (if present), and is equivalent to calling SDL\_\-SetPalette with the flags set to (SDL\_\-LOGPAL $|$ SDL\_\-PHYSPAL).  

When 'surface' is the surface associated with the current display, the display colormap will be updated with the requested colors. If SDL\_\-HWPALETTE was set in \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a961f7efdc2a7ec3860e93140853092f7}{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode()} flags, \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_ad3dd27ac574c77908bc25298e847f77a}{SDL\_\-SetColors()} will always return 1, and the palette is guaranteed to be set the way you desire, even if the window colormap has to be warped or run under emulation. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
extern DECLSPEC int SDLCALL SDL_SetColors(SDL_Surface *surface, SDL_Color *colors
      , int firstcolor, int ncolors)
\end{DoxyCode}
 

/$\ast$ Create a display surface with a grayscale palette

Palettized (8-\/bit) screen surfaces with the SDL\_\-HWPALETTE flag have two palettes, a logical palette that is used for mapping blits to/from the surface and a physical palette (that determines how the hardware will map the colors to the display). SDL\_\-BlitSurface always uses the logical palette when blitting surfaces (if it has to convert between surface pixel formats). Because of this, it is often useful to modify only one or the other palette to achieve various special color effects (e.g., screen fading, color flashes, screen dimming).

This function can modify either the logical or physical palette by specifing SDL\_\-LOGPAL or SDL\_\-PHYSPALthe in the flags parameter.

When surface is the surface associated with the current display, the display colormap will be updated with the requested colors. If SDL\_\-HWPALETTE was set in SDL\_\-SetVideoMode flags, SDL\_\-SetPalette will always return 1, and the palette is guaranteed to be set the way you desire, even if the window colormap has to be warped or run under emulation. 

The color components of a \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___color}{SDL\_\-Color} structure are 8-\/bits in size, giving you a total of 2563=16777216 colors. 

'flags' is one or both of: SDL\_\-LOGPAL -\/-\/ set logical palette, which controls how blits are mapped to/from the surface, SDL\_\-PHYSPAL -\/-\/ set physical palette, which controls how pixels look on the screen Only screens have physical palettes. Separate change of physical/logical palettes is only possible if the screen has SDL\_\-HWPALETTE set. /p$>$

\hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_ad3dd27ac574c77908bc25298e847f77a}{SDL\_\-SetColors()} is equivalent to calling this function with flags = (SDL\_\-LOGPAL$|$SDL\_\-PHYSPAL). 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
extern DECLSPEC int SDLCALL SDL_SetPalette(SDL_Surface *surface, int flags, 
      SDL_Color *colors, int firstcolor, int ncolors)
\end{DoxyCode}

 SDL_CreateRGBSurface(SDL_SWSURFACE, width, height, 32,
                        rmask, gmask, bmask, amask)
\end{DoxyCode}


Create an empty \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___surface}{SDL\_\-Surface}. 

Allocate an empty surface (must be called after \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a961f7efdc2a7ec3860e93140853092f7}{SDL\_\-SetVideoMode(int, int, int, int)}). 

If depth is 8 bits an empty palette is allocated for the surface, otherwise a 'packed-\/pixel' \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___pixel_format}{SDL\_\-PixelFormat} is created using the \mbox{[}RGBA\mbox{]}mask's provided (see \hyperlink{struct_s_d_l___pixel_format}{SDL\_\-PixelFormat}). The flags specifies the type of surface that should be created, it is an OR'd combination of the following possible values. \begin{TabularC}{2}
\hline
SDL\_\-SWSURFACE} &SDL will create the surface in system memory. This improves the performance of pixel level access, however you may not be able to take advantage of some types of hardware blitting.   \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-HWSURFACE} &SDL will attempt to create the surface in video memory. This will allow SDL to take advantage of Video-\/$>$Video blits (which are often accelerated).   \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-SRCCOLORKEY} &This flag turns on colourkeying for blits from this surface. If SDL\_\-HWSURFACE is also specified and colourkeyed blits are hardware-\/accelerated, then SDL will attempt to place the surface in video memory. Use \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a6143709fbf5b39f734e9de78cfa1d6c8}{SDL\_\-SetColorKey(IntPtr, int, int)} to set or clear this flag after surface creation.   \\\cline{1-2}
SDL\_\-SRCALPHA} &This flag turns on alpha-\/blending for blits from this surface. If SDL\_\-HWSURFACE is also specified and alpha-\/blending blits are hardware-\/accelerated, then the surface will be placed in video memory if possible. Use \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a77f6839de15f85b6c5afd9174894a41a}{SDL\_\-SetAlpha(IntPtr, int, byte)} to set or clear this flag after surface creation.   \\\cline{1-2}
\end{TabularC}


{\bfseries Note:} If an alpha-\/channel is specified (that is, if Amask is nonzero), then the SDL\_\-SRCALPHA flag is automatically set. You may remove this flag by calling \hyperlink{_sdl_8cs_a77f6839de15f85b6c5afd9174894a41a}{SDL\_\-SetAlpha(IntPtr, int, byte)} after surface creation. 

Binds to C-\/function call in SDL\_\-video.h: 
\begin{DoxyCode}
SDL_Surface *SDL_CreateRGBSurface(Uint32 flags, int width, int height, int depth,
       Uint32 Rmask, Uint32 Gmask, Uint32 Bmask, Uint32 Amask)
\end{DoxyCode}
